<div><tool-result call-id="toolu_01ATyrmE9gfEZkQSALMq5sLc"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"status":"success","result":{"type":"text","value":"[File: 23.4KB, 917 lines, showing lines 101-300 (truncated)]\n   101→mxl_renter <- logitr(\n...[truncated, total 5934 chars]"},"resultPreview":{"type":"code","value":"[File: 23.4KB, 917 lines, showing lines 101-300 (truncated)]\nmxl_renter <- logitr(\n  data    = df_model %>% filter(Own == \"Renter\") ,\n  outcome = \"choice\",\n  obsID   = \"obsID\",\n  panelID = \"panelID\",\n  pars    = c(\"dist_green\", \"dist_shops\", \"dist_trans\", \"parking\", \"price_num\"),\n  randPars = c(dist_green = 'n', dist_shops = 'n', dist_trans = 'n', parking = 'n'),\n  numMultiStarts = 10,\n  drawType = 'sobol',\n  numDraws = 100,\n  correlation = TRUE\n)\n\nscreenreg(list(mxl_owner,mxl_renter))\n\n\nsaveRDS(mxl_renter, here(\"output/models\", \"mxl_renter_base.rds\"))\n\nsaveRDS(mxl_owner, here(\"output/models\", \"mxl_owner_base.rds\"))\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n## Create tables ----\n\nmxl_renter <- readRDS(here(\"output/models\", \"mxl_renter_base.rds\"))\n\nmxl_owner<- readRDS(here(\"output/models\", \"mxl_owner_base.rds\"))\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n# function\n\ncompute_bic <- function(model) {\n  ll <- as.numeric(logLik(model))\n  k  <- attr(logLik(model), \"df\")\n  n  <- tryCatch(model$n$obs, error = function(e) NA)\n  if (is.na(n)) return(NA)\n  k * log(n) - 2 * ll\n}\n\n\n\n\n# 0) Tidy outputs\nt_renter <- tidy(mxl_renter)\nt_owner  <- tidy(mxl_owner)\n\n# MEANS = terms not beginning with sd_\nmeans_renter <- t_renter %>% filter(!str_starts(term, \"sd_\"))\nmeans_owner  <- t_owner  %>% filter(!str_starts(term, \"sd_\"))\n\n# SDs = diagonal random parameter SD terms: sd_x_x\nextract_diagonal <- function(df) {\n  df %>%\n    filter(str_starts(term, \"sd_\")) %>%\n    mutate(attr = str_match(term, \"^sd_(.*)_\\\\1$\")[,2]) %>%\n    filter(!is.na(attr))\n}\n\nsds_renter <- extract_diagonal(t_renter)\nsds_owner  <- extract_diagonal(t_owner)\n\n# Attribute order taken from renter means\nattr_terms <- means_renter$term\n\n\n# renter\ncoef_renter <- means_renter$estimate[match(attr_terms, means_renter$term)]\nse_renter   <- means_renter$std.error[match(attr_terms, means_renter$term)]\np_renter    <- means_renter$p.value[match(attr_terms, means_renter$term)]\n\nsd_renter   <- sds_renter$estimate[match(attr_terms, sds_renter$attr)]\nsd_renter_se <- sds_renter$std.error[match(attr_terms, sds_renter$attr)]\nsd_renter_p  <- sds_renter$p.value[match(attr_terms, sds_renter$attr)]\n\n# owner\ncoef_owner <- means_owner$estimate[match(attr_terms, means_owner$term)]\nse_owner   <- means_owner$std.error[match(attr_terms, means_owner$term)]\np_owner    <- means_owner$p.value[match(attr_terms, means_owner$term)]\n\nsd_owner   <- sds_owner$estimate[match(attr_terms, sds_owner$attr)]\nsd_owner_se <- sds_owner$std.error[match(attr_terms, sds_owner$attr)]\nsd_owner_p  <- sds_owner$p.value[match(attr_terms, sds_owner$attr)]\n\n\n# Compute LR test for renter model\nll_renter     <- as.numeric(logLik(mxl_renter))\nll_null_renter <- mxl_renter$nullLogLik\nk_renter      <- attr(logLik(mxl_renter), \"df\")\n\nlr_renter     <- -2 * (ll_null_renter - ll_renter)\np_lr_renter   <- pchisq(lr_renter, df = k_renter, lower.tail = FALSE)\n\n# Compute LR test for owner model\nll_owner       <- as.numeric(logLik(mxl_owner))\nll_null_owner  <- mxl_owner$nullLogLik\nk_owner        <- attr(logLik(mxl_owner), \"df\")\n\nlr_owner       <- -2 * (ll_null_owner - ll_owner)\np_lr_owner     <- pchisq(lr_owner, df = k_owner, lower.tail = FALSE)\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n# Create texreg objects for each column\n\n# RENTER MEAN (Model 1)\nm_renter_mean <- createTexreg(\n  coef.names = attr_terms,\n  coef       = coef_renter,\n  se         = se_renter,\n  pvalues    = p_renter,\n  gof.names  = c(\n    \"Num. obs.\",\n    \"Log Likelihood\",\n    \"AIC\",\n    \"BIC\",\n    \"McFadden R2\",\n    paste0(\"LR χ² (df=\", k_renter, \")\"),\n    \"p-value (LR)\"\n  ),\n  gof = c(\n    mxl_renter$n$obs,\n    ll_renter,\n    AIC(mxl_renter),\n    compute_bic(mxl_renter),\n    1 - (ll_renter / ll_null_renter),\n    lr_renter,\n    p_lr_renter\n  ),\n  gof.decimal = c(FALSE, TRUE, TRUE, TRUE, TRUE, TRUE, TRUE)\n)\n\n\n# OWNER MEAN (Model 3)\nm_owner_mean <- createTexreg(\n  coef.names = attr_terms,\n  coef       = coef_owner,\n  se         = se_owner,\n  pvalues    = p_owner,\n  gof.names  = c(\n    \"Num. obs.\",\n    \"Log Likelihood\",\n    \"AIC\",\n    \"BIC\",\n    \"McFadden R2\",\n    paste0(\"LR χ² (df=\", k_owner, \")\"),\n    \"p-value (LR)\"\n  ),\n  gof = c(\n    mxl_owner$n$obs,\n    ll_owner,\n    AIC(mxl_owner),\n    compute_bic(mxl_owner),\n    1 - (ll_owner / ll_null_owner),\n    lr_owner,\n    p_lr_owner\n  ),\n  gof.decimal = c(FALSE, TRUE, TRUE, TRUE, TRUE, TRUE, TRUE)\n)\n\n# OWNER SD\nm_owner_sd <- createTexreg(\n  coef.names = attr_terms,\n  coef       = sd_owner,\n  se         = sd_owner_se,\n  pvalues    = sd_owner_p\n)\n\nm_renter_sd <- createTexreg(\n  coef.names = attr_terms,\n  coef       = sd_renter,\n  se         = sd_renter_se,"},"elapsedMs":64}</script></tool-result></div>

<div><thinking id="thinking-1774861407184-2r61u">
Good. Now I understand the structure:

- `mxl_age_own.rds` / `mxl_age_rent.rds`: Models with `High_age` (above median age) interaction terms (`green5km_High_age`, etc.)
- `mxl_old_owner.rds` / `mxl_old_renter.rds`: Models with `Old` (age ≥ 72) interaction terms (`green5km_Old`, etc.)

So for Table 5, the paper uses one of these. Looking at `table_7_interactions.R` which uses `mxl_age_own.rds` and `mxl_age_rent.rds`, that's likely the one for the paper's "interaction with age" table.


Now I need to check what's in the sex interaction models by looking at `interaction_regs_owner_sex.R` to see what gets saved in `mxl_sex_owner.rds` and `mxl_sex_renter.rds`.
</thinking></div>

scaler\r  if (group != \"base\") {\r    if (any(terms == a_g_term)) grad[terms == a_g_term] <- -1 / C * scaler\r    if (any(terms == c_g_term)) grad[terms == c_g_term] <- (A / (C^2)) * scaler\r  }\r  \r  Vsub <- V[terms, terms, drop = FALSE]\r  var  <- as.numeric(t(grad) %*% Vsub %*% grad)\r  if (!is.finite(var) || var < 0) return(c(val, NA_real_, NA_real_))\r  se   <- ----\nmxl_renter <- readRDS(here(\"output/models\", \"mxl_renter_base.rds\"))\nmxl_owner  <- readRDS(here(\"output/models\", \"mxl_owner_base.rds\"))\n\n# Scalers (10 % of median monthly housing cost -> SEK/month) ----\nscaler_rent <- 0.10 * 9000   # = 900 SEK\nscaler_own  <- 0.10 * 10000  # = 1000 SEK\n\nprice_term <- \"price_num\"\n\n# Delta-method MWTP and MRS ----\ncompute_mwtp_mrs <- function(model, scale_value) {\n  t_means <- tidy(model) |> filter(!str_starts(term, \"sd_\"))\n  vc      <- vcov(model)\n  attrs   <- setdiff(t_means$term, price_term)\n\n  purrr::map_dfr(attrs, function(a) {\n    beta_a <- t_means$estimate[t_means$term == a]\n    beta_p <- t_means$estimate[t_means$term == price_term]\n\n    mrs  <- -beta_a / beta_p\n    mwtp <- mrs * scale_value\n\n    # Delta method SE\n    grad          <- c(-1 / beta_p, beta_a / (beta_p^2))\n    names(grad)   <- c(a, price_term)\n    V_sub         <- vc[c(a, price_term), c(a, price_term)]\n    se_mrs        <- as.numeric(sqrt(t(grad) %*% V_sub %*% grad))\n    se_mwtp       <- se_mrs * scale_value\n\n    tibble(\n      attribute = a,\n      mrs       = as.numeric(mrs),\n      mrs_lo    = mrs - 1.96 * se_mrs,\n      mrs_hi    = mrs + 1.96 * se_mrs,\n      mwtp      = round(as.numeric(mwtp), 0),\n      mwtp_lo   = round(mwtp - 1.96 * se_mwtp, 0),\n      mwtp_hi   = round(mwtp + 1.96 * se_mwtp, 0)\n    )\n  })\n}\n\nmwtp_rent <- compute_mwtp_mrs(mxl_renter, scaler_rent)\nmwtp_own  <- compute_mwtp_mrs(mxl_owner,  scaler_own)\n\n# Attribute labels ----\nlabel_map <- c(\n  \"dist_green5km\"                 = \"Green space: 5 km (vs 15 km)\",\n  \"dist_green500 meter\"           = \"Green space: 500 m (vs 15 km)\",\n  \"dist_shops5km\"                 = \"Shops: 5 km (vs 15 km)\",\n (vs 900 m)\",\n  \"parkingreserverad garageplats\" = \"Parking: reserved garage (vs none)\",\n  \"parkingreserverad P-plats\"     = \"Parking: reserved space (vs none)\"\n)\n\n# Build display table ----\nfmt_mrs  <- function(v, lo, hi) sprintf(\"%.2f (%.2f, %.2f)\", v, lo, hi)\nfmt_mwtp <- function(v, lo, hi) sprintf(\"%d (%d, %d)\", v, lo, hi)\n\ndisplay <- tibble(\n  Attribute        = label_map[mwtp_own$attribute],\n  `Owner MRS`      = fmt_mrs(mwtp_own$mrs, mwtp_own$mrs_lo, mwtp_own$mrs_hi),\n  `Owner MWTP`     = fmt_mwtp(mwtp_own$mwtp, mwtp_own$mwtp_lo, mwtp_own$mwtp_hi),\n  `Renter MRS`     = fmt_mrs(mwtp_rent$mrs[match(mwtp_own$attribute, mwtp_rent$attribute)],\n                              mwtp_rent$mrs_lo[match(mwtp_own$attribute, mwtp_rent$attribute)],\n                              mwtp_rent$mrs_hi[match(mwtp_own$attribute, mwtp_rent$attribute)]),\n  `Renter MWTP`    = fmt_mwtp(mwtp_rent$mwtp[match(mwtp_own$attribute, mwtp_rent$attribute)],\n substitution (unitless ratio), estimated via delta method. \n95% confidence intervals in parentheses.   = c(NA, \"green5km_G65_74\", \"green500_G65_74\",\r               NA, \"shops5km_G65_74\", \"shops500_G65_74\",\r               NA, \"trans600_G65_74\", \"trans300_G65_74\",\r               NA,   ~ \"G75p\",\r  TRUE         ~ \"\"\r)\r\r# --- Function to compute WTP from a fitted model --------------------------\rcompute_wtp_df <- function(model, group_label) {\r  coef_df <- tidy(model) %>%\r    mutate(conf.low = estimate - 1.96 * std.error,\r           conf.high = estimate + 1.96 * std.error)\r  \r  coefs <- setNames(coef_df$estimate, coef_df$term)\r  \r  get_wtp <- function(base, interaction = NULL, group = \"55-64\") {\r    if (!(base %in% names(coefs))) {\r      return(tibble(estimate = NA_real_, conf.low = NA_real_, conf.high = NA_real_))\r    }\r    \r    est <- coefs[[base]]\r    se  <- coef_df %>% filter(term == base) %>% pull(std.error)\r    \r    if (!is.null(interaction) && !is.na(interaction) && interaction %in% names(coefs)) {\r      est <- est + coefs[[interaction]]\r      se_int <- coef_df %>% filter(term == interaction) %>% pull(std.error)\r      se <- sqrt(se^2 + se_int^2)\r      \r      price_term <- paste0(\"price_\", group_suffix(group))\r      if (price_term %in% names(coefs)) {\r        denom <- coefs[[\"price_num\"]] + coefs[[price_term]]\r      } else {\r        denom <- coefs[[\"price_num\"]]\r      }\r    }   \r    tibble(estimate = wtp_sek,\r           conf.low = wtp_sek - se_wtp,\r           conf.high = wtp_sek + se_wtp)\r  }\r  \r  expand.grid(\r    attribute = attr_map$display,\r    age_group = c(\"55-64\", \"65-74\", \"75+\"),\r    stringsAsFactors = FALSE\r  ) %>%\r    left_join(attr_map, by = c(\"attribute\" = \"display\")) %>%\r    rowwise() %>%\r    mutate(\r      interaction_term = age_group))\r    ) %>%\r    unnest(wtp_info) %>%\r    mutate(model_group = group_label)\r}\r\r# --- Compute for both models ---\rplot_df_own  <- compute_wtp_df(mxl_own,  \"Owners\")\rplot_df_rent <- case_when(\r      grepl(\"garage\", attribute, ignore.case = TRUE) ~ \"Parking: garage (ref: none)\",\r      grepl(\"reserved\", attribute, ignore.case = TRUE) ~ \"Parking: reserved (ref: none)\",\r      grepl(\"300m\", attribute, ignore.case = TRUE) ~ \"Transit stop: 300 m (ref: 900 m)\",\r      grepl(\"600m\", attribute, ignore.case = TRUE) ~ \"Transit stop: 600 m (ref: 900 m)\",\r      grepl(\"500m\", attribute, ignore.case = TRUE) & grepl(\"shop\", attribute, ignore.case = TRUE) ~ \"Shops: 500 m (ref: 15 km)\",\r      grepl(\"5km\", attribute, ignore.case = TRUE) & grepl(\"shop\", attribute, ignore.case = TRUE) ~ \"Shops: 5 km (ref: 15 km)\",\r      grepl(\"500m\", attribute, ignore.case = TRUE) & grepl(\"green\", attribute, ignore.case = TRUE) ~ \"Green space: 500 m (ref: 15 km)\",\r      grepl(\"5km\", attribute, ignore.case = TRUE) & grepl(\"green\", attribute, ignore.case = TRUE) ~ \"Green space: 5 km (ref: 15 km)\",\r      TRUE ~ NA_character_\r    )\r  ) %>%\r  filter(!is.na(attribute))  # remove reference-level rows\r\r# --- Factor order for attributes ---\rattribute_levels <- c(\r  \"Parking: garage (ref: none)\",\r  \"Parking: reserved (ref: none)\",\r  \"Transit stop: 300 m (ref: 900 m)\",\r  \"Transit stop: 600 m (ref: 900 m)\",\r  \"Shops: 500 m (ref: 15 km)\",\r  \"Shops: 5 km (ref: 15 km)\",\r  \"Green space: 500 m (ref: 15 km)\",\r  \"Green space: 5 km (ref: 15 km)\"\r)\r\rplot_df$attribute <- factor(plot_df$attribute, levels = rev(attribute_levels))\r\r# --- Shared color palette ---\rage_colors <- c(\"55-64\" = \"#1b9e77\", \"65-74\" = \"#d95f02\", \"75+\" = \"#7570b3\")\r\r# --- Shared x-axis limits ---\rxlims <- range(c(plot_df$conf.low, plot_df$conf.high), na.rm = TRUE)\rxlims <- c(floor(xlims[1] / 100) * 100, ceiling(xlims[2] / 100) * 100)\r\r# --- Plot function ---\rplot_wtp <- function(df, title) {\r  ggplot(df, aes(x = estimate, y = attribute, color = age_group)) +\r    geom_point(position = position_dodge(width = 0.6), size = 3) +\r    geom_errorbarh(aes(xmin = conf.low, xmax = conf.high),\r                   position = position_dodge(width = 0.6), height = 0.4,\r                   linewidth = 1) +\r   limits = c(-200, 1200),\r      breaks = seq(-200, 1200, by = 200)\r    ) +\r  \r  \r    labs(x = \"WTP (SEK/month)\", y = NULL, color = \"Age group\", title = title) +\r    theme_minimal(base_size = 14) +\r    theme(\r      axis.text.y = element_text(size = 15),\r      axis.title.x = element_text(size = 13),\r      plot.title = element_text(size = 14, face = \"bold\", hjust = 0.5),\r      legend.position = \"bottom\",\r      legend.title = element_text(size = 13),\r      legend.text = element_text(size = 13),\r      panel.grid.minor = element_blank()\r      \r    )\r}\r\r# --- Create          return(\"G75p\")\n  if (term == cost_name)              return(\"price\")\n  if (grepl(\"^price_\", term))         return(\"price_inter\")\n  \"other\"\n}\n\nterm_attr <- function(term) {\n  if (term %in% main_attrs)                    return(term)\n  if (term %in% names(interaction_to_base))    return(interaction_to_base[[term]])\n  NA_character_\n}\n\nmwtp_for_attr_group <- function(attr, group, tidy_df, V, scaler, cost_name) {\n  beta_a   <- grab_term(tidy_df, attr)[1]\n  beta_c   <- grab_term(tidy_df, cost_name)[1]\n  a_g_term <- if (group == \"base\") NA_character_\n    else names(interaction_to_base)[interaction_to_base == attr & grepl(group, names(interaction_to_base))]\n  c_g_term <- if (group == \"base\") NA_character_\n    else 0\n  beta_c_g <- if (length(c_g_term) && !is.na(c_g_term)) grab_term(tidy_df, c_g_term)[1] else 0\n\n  if (any(is.na(c(beta_a, beta_c)))) return(c(NA_real_, NA_real_, NA_real_))\n\n  A   <- beta_a + ifelse(group == \"base\", 0, beta_a_g)\n  C   <- beta_c + ifelse(group == \"base\", 0, beta_c_g)\n  val <- -(A / C) * scaler\n\n  terms <- c(attr, cost_name,\n             if (group != \"base\" && !is.na(a_g_term)) a_g_term else NULL,\n             if (group != \"base\" && !is.na(c_g_term)) c_g_term else NULL)\n  terms <- terms[!is.na(terms) & nzchar(terms)]\n  if (is.null(V) || !all(terms %in% rownames(V))) return(c(val, NA_real_, NA_real_))\n\n  grad <- numeric(length(terms))\n  grad[terms == attr]      <- -1 / C * scaler\n  grad[terms == cost_name] <- (A / C^2) * scaler\n  if (group != \"base\") {\n    if (any(terms == a_g_term)) grad[terms == a_g_term] <- -1 / C * scaler\n    if (any(terms == c_g_term)) grad[terms == c_g_term] <- (A / C^2) * scaler\n  }\n\n  Vsub <- V[terms, terms, drop = FALSE]\n  var  <- as.numeric(t(grad) %*% Vsub %*% grad)\n  if (!is.finite(var) || var < 0) return(c(val, NA_real_, NA_real_))\n  se   <- sqrt(var)\n  pval <- 2 * pnorm(-abs(val / se))\n  c(val, se, pval)\n}\n\ncompute_bic <- function(model) {\n  ll <- as.numeric(logLik(model))\n  k  <- attr(logLik(model), \"df\")\n  n  <- tryCatch(model$n$obs, error = function(e) NA)\n  if (is.na(n)) return(NA_real_)\n  k * log(n) - 2 * ll\n}\n\nlr_bits <- function(model) {\n  ll  <- as.numeric(logLik(model))\n  ll0 <- tryCatch(model$nullLogLik, error = function(e) NA_real_)\n  k   <- attr(logLik(model), \"df\")\n  if (is.na(ll0)) return(list(lr = NA_real_, p = NA_real_, k = k))\n  lr  <- -2 * (ll0 - ll)\n  list(lr = lr, p = pchisq(lr, df = k, lower.tail = FALSE), k = k)\n}\n\n# Build texreg object pair for one model ----\nbuild_pair <- function(model, scaler, cost_name) {\n  tdf <- broom::tidy(model)\n  V   <- tryCatch(vcov(model), error = function(e) NULL)\n\n  coef_vals <- setNames(rep(NA_real_, length(coef_rows)), coef_rows)\n  se_vals   <- coef_vals\n  p_vals    <- coef_vals\n  mwtp_vals <- coef_vals\n  mwtp_se   <- coef_vals\n  mwtp_p    <- coef_vals\n\n  for (term in coef_rows) {\n    x <- grab_term(tdf, term)\n    coef_vals[term] <- x[1]; se_vals[term] <- x[2]; p_vals[term] <- x[3]\n  }\n\n  for (term in coef_rows) {\n    g <- term_group(term)\n    if (g %in% c(\"price\", \"price_inter\", \"other\")) next\n    a   <- term_attr(term)\n    out <- mwtp_for_attr_group(a, ifelse(g == \"base\", \"base\", g), tdf, V, scaler, cost_name)\n    mwtp_vals[term] <- out[1]; mwtp_se[term] <- out[2]; mwtp_p[term] <- out[3]\n  }\n\n  ll  <- as.numeric(logLik(model))\n  ll0 <- tryCatch(model$nullLogLik, error = function(e) NA_real_)\n  lr  <- lr_bits(model)\n  gof_n <- c(\"Num. obs.\", \"Log Likelihood\", \"AIC\", \"BIC\", \"McFadden R\\u00b2\",\n             paste0(\"LR \\u03c7\\u00b2 (df=\", lr$k, \")\"), \"p-value (LR)\")\n  gof_v <- c(tryCatch(model$n$obs, error = function(e) NA_integer_),\n             ll, AIC(model), compute_bic(model),\n             if (!is.na(ll0)) 1 - ll / ll0 else NA_real_,\n             lr$lr, lr$p)\n  gof_d <- c(FALSE, TRUE, TRUE, TRUE, TRUE, TRUE, TRUE)\n\n  m_coef <- createTexreg(\n    coef.names  = pretty_labels,\n    coef        = as.numeric(coef_vals),\n    se          = as.numeric(se_vals),\n    pvalues     = as.numeric(p_vals),\n    gof.names   = gof_n,\n    gof         = gof_v,\n    gof.decimal = gof_d\n  )\n\n  m_mwtp <- createTexreg(\n    coef.names = pretty_labels,\n    coef       = as.numeric(mwtp_vals),\n    se         = as.numeric(mwtp_se),\n    pvalues    = as.numeric(mwtp_p)\n  )\n\n  list(m_coef = m_coef, m_mwtp = m_mwtp)\n}\n\n# Build and render ----\nown  <- build_pair(mxl_own,  scaler, cost_name)\nrent <- build_pair(mxl_rent, scaler, cost_name)\n\nhtmlreg(\n  list(own$m_coef, own$m_mwtp, rent$m_coef, rent$m_mwtp),\n  custom.header      = list(\"Owners\" = 1:2, \"Renters\" = 3:4),\n  custom.model.names = c(\"Coef.\", \"MWTP\", \"Coef.\", \"MWTP\"),\n  custom.coef.names  = pretty_labels,\n  digits             = 2,\n  stars              = c(0.001, 0.01, 0.05),\n  na.replace         = \"\\u2013\",\n  caption            = \"Table 5. Interaction regression with age (reference: age 55\\u201364)\",\n  caption.above      = TRUE,\n  file               = here(\"output/tables\", \"table_05_interaction_age.html\")\n)\n\nmessage(\"Table 5 saved to output/tables/table_05_interaction_age.html\")\n"}}</script></tool-call></div>

return(\"price\")\n  if (grepl(\"^price_\", term))    return(\"price_inter\")\n  \"other\"\n}\n\nterm_attr <- function(term) {\n  if (term %in% main_attrs)                 return(term)\n  if (term %in% names(interaction_to_base)) return(interaction_to_base[[term]])\n  NA_character_\n}\n\nmwtp_for_attr_group <- function(attr, group, tidy_df, V, scaler, cost_name) {\n  beta_a   <- grab_term(tidy_df, attr)[1]\n  beta_c   <- grab_term(tidy_df, cost_name)[1]\n  a_g_term <- if (group == \"base\") NA_character_\n    else names(interaction_to_base)[interaction_to_base == attr & grepl(group, names(interaction_to_base))]\n  c_g_term <- if (group == \"base\") NA_character_\n    else names(interaction_to_base)[interaction_to_base == cost_name & grepl(group, names(interaction_to_base))]\n  beta_a_g <- if (length(a_g_term) && !is.na(a_g_term)) grab_term(tidy_df, a_g_term)[1] else 0\n  beta_c_g <- if (length(c_g_term) && !is.na(c_g_term)) grab_term(tidy_df, c_g_term)[1] else 0\n\n  if (any(is.na(c(beta_a, beta_c)))) return(c(NA_real_, NA_real_, NA_real_))\n\n  A   <- beta_a + ifelse(group == \"base\", 0, beta_a_g)\n  C   <- beta_c + ifelse(group == \"base\", 0, beta_c_g)\n  val <- -(A / C) * scaler\n\n  terms <- c(attr, cost_name,\n             if (group != \"base\" && !is.na(a_g_term)) a_g_term else NULL,\n             if (group != \"base\" && !is.na(c_g_term)) c_g_term else NULL)\n  terms <- terms[!is.na(terms) & nzchar(terms)]\n  if (is.null(V) || !all(terms %in% rownames(V))) return(c(val, NA_real_, NA_real_))\n\n  grad <- numeric(length(terms))\n  grad[terms == attr]      <- -1 / C * scaler\n  grad[terms == cost_name] <- (A / C^2) * scaler\n  if (group != \"base\") {\n    if (any(terms == a_g_term)) grad[terms == a_g_term] <- -1 / C * scaler\n    if (any(terms == c_g_term)) grad[terms == c_g_term] <- (A / C^2) * scaler\n  }\n\n  Vsub <- V[terms, terms, drop = FALSE]\n  var  <- as.numeric(t(grad) %*% Vsub %*% grad)\n  if (!is.finite(var) || var < 0) return(c(val, NA_real_, NA_real_))\n  se   <- sqrt(var)\n  pval <- 2 * pnorm(-abs(val / se))\n  c(val, se, pval)\n}\n\ncompute_bic <- function(model) {\n  ll <- as.numeric(logLik(model))\n  k  <- attr(logLik(model), \"df\")\n  n  <- tryCatch(model$n$obs, error = function(e) NA)\n  if (is.na(n)) return(NA_real_)\n  k * log(n) - 2 * ll\n}\n\nlr_bits <- function(model) {\n  ll  <- as.numeric(logLik(model))\n  ll0 <- tryCatch(model$nullLogLik, error = function(e) NA_real_)\n  k   <- attr(logLik(model), \"df\")\n  if (is.na(ll0)) return(list(lr = NA_real_, p = NA_real_, k = k))\n  lr  <- -2 * (ll0 - ll)\n  list(lr = lr, p = pchisq(lr, df = k, lower.tail = FALSE), k = k)\n}\n\n# Build texreg object pair for one model ----\nbuild_pair <- function(model, scaler, cost_name) {\n  tdf <- broom::tidy(model)\n  V   <- tryCatch(vcov(model), error = function(e) NULL)\n\n  coef_vals <- setNames(rep(NA_real_, length(coef_rows)), coef_rows)\n  se_vals   <- coef_vals\n  p_vals    <- coef_vals\n  mwtp_vals <- coef_vals\n  mwtp_se   <- coef_vals\n  mwtp_p    <- coef_vals\n\n  for (term in coef_rows) {\n    x <- grab_term(tdf, term)\n    coef_vals[term] <- x[1]; se_vals[term] <- x[2]; p_vals[term] <- x[3]\n  }\n\n  for (term in coef_rows) {\n    g <- term_group(term)\n    if (g %in% c(\"price\", \"price_inter\", \"other\")) next\n    a   <- term_attr(term)\n    out <- mwtp_for_attr_group(a, ifelse(g == \"base\", \"base\", g), tdf, V, scaler, cost_name)\n    mwtp_vals[term] <- out[1]; mwtp_se[term] <- out[2]; mwtp_p[term] <- out[3]\n  }\n\n  ll  <- as.numeric(logLik(model))\n  ll0 <- tryCatch(model$nullLogLik, error = function(e) NA_real_)\n  lr  <- lr_bits(model)\n  gof_n <- c(\"Num. obs.\", \"Log Likelihood\", \"AIC\", \"BIC\", \"McFadden R\\u00b2\",\n             paste0(\"LR \\u03c7\\u00b2 (df=\", lr$k, \")\"), \"p-value (LR)\")\n  gof_v <- c(tryCatch(model$n$obs, error = function(e) NA_integer_),\n             ll, AIC(model), compute_bic(model),\n             if (!is.na(ll0)) 1 - ll / ll0 else NA_real_,\n             lr$lr, lr$p)\n  gof_d <- c(FALSE, TRUE, TRUE, TRUE, TRUE, TRUE, TRUE)\n\n  m_coef <- createTexreg(\n    coef.names  = pretty_labels,\n    coef        = as.numeric(coef_vals),\n    se          = as.numeric(se_vals),\n    pvalues     = as.numeric(p_vals),\n    gof.names   = gof_n,\n    gof         = gof_v,\n    gof.decimal = gof_d\n  )\n\n  m_mwtp <- createTexreg(\n    coef.names = pretty_labels,\n    coef       = as.numeric(mwtp_vals),\n    se         = as.numeric(mwtp_se),\n    pvalues    = as.numeric(mwtp_p)\n  )\n\n  list(m_coef = m_coef, m_mwtp = m_mwtp)\n}\n\n# Build and render ----\nown  <- build_pair(mxl_own,  scaler, cost_name)\nrent <- build_pair(mxl_rent, scaler, cost_name)\n\nhtmlreg(\n  list(own$m_coef, own$m_mwtp, rent$m_coef, rent$m_mwtp),\n  custom.header      = list(\"Owners\" = 1:2, \"Renters\" = 3:4),\n  custom.model.names = c(\"Coef.\", \"MWTP\", \"Coef.\", \"MWTP\"),\n  custom.coef.names  = pretty_labels,\n  digits             = 2,\n  stars              = c(0.001, 0.01, 0.05),\n  na.replace         = \"\\u2013\",\n  caption            = \"Table 6. Interaction regression with sex (reference: women)\",\n  caption.above      = TRUE,\n  file               = here(\"output/tables\", \"table_06_interaction_sex.html\")\n)\n\nmessage(\"Table 6 saved to output/tables/table_06_interaction_sex.html\")\n"}}</script></tool-call></div>

All 8 scripts are in place. Here's a summary of what was built:

---

**New structure:** `scripts/paper/tables/` contains 8 clean, focused scripts:

| Script | What it does | Output |
|---|---|---|
| `00_data_prep.R` | Shared data loading + cleaning; `source()` from any table script that needs survey data | — |
| `table_01_attributes.R` | Hard-coded attribute/levels table (no data needed) | `flextable` → HTML |
| `table_02_sample_characteristics.R` | Sample characteristics by Owner/Renter with p-values | `flextable` → HTML |
| `table_03_baseline_mxl.R` | Loads `mxl_owner_base.rds` + `mxl_renter_base.rds` → 4-column table (Coef + SD per group) | `htmlreg` → HTML |
| `table_04_mwtp.R` | Same baseline models → MRS (95% CI) + MWTP (SEK/month) | `flextable` → HTML |
| `table_05_interaction_age.R` | Loads `mxl_age_own/rent.rds` → age group (65–74, 75+) interactions | `htmlreg` → HTML |
| `table_06_interaction_sex.R` | Loads `mxl_sex_owner/renter.rds` → Men interaction | `htmlreg` → HTML |
| `table_07_interaction_health.R` | Loads `mxl_health_own/rent.rds` → Good health interaction | `htmlreg` → HTML |

All outputs go to `output/tables/`. The HTML files open in Word directly (File → Open) or can be copy-pasted into a Word document. No existing scripts were touched.

One thing to flag: for Table 2, the script calls `distinct(panelID, .keep_all = TRUE)` to deduplicate to one row per respondent. If your `df_model.rds` is already at the respondent level (not choice-occasion level), you can remove that line. Run the script and check the N before and after to confirm.

I'll suggest some follow-up steps below.


<span class="suggestion">Run the table scripts interactively to confirm they produce the correct outputs, starting with `table_03_baseline_mxl.R` as the simplest sanity check.</span>


<span class="suggestion">Check whether the `mxl_age_own/rent.rds` models (which use a median-age binary split) match what's shown in the Word doc — the paper may intend the age-group (55–64 / 65–74 / 75+) split instead, in which case we'd need to verify the interaction term names in the saved models.</span>


<span class="suggestion">Combine all 7 HTML outputs into a single Word document using a small R script with the `officer` package.</span>

<div><thinking id="thinking-1774865126614-yqqcf">
The `extra.col` p-value function doesn't work with 3 groups (it calls `t.test(y ~ g)` which needs exactly 2 levels). I need to either remove the p-value column when overall is included, or fix the pvalue function to only compare the two tenure groups.

Actually, the p-value column is between Owner and Renter, not involving Overall. Looking at how `table1` handles this — with `overall = "Overall"`, the strata are now Owner, Renter, and Overall (3 groups). But the p-value function uses all strata.
 
Let me reconsider how `table1` passes data to `extra.col` — it should only receive the two stratification groups, not the overall column. So the "exactly 2 levels" error must be coming from somewhere else in how the function is being called.

Actually, I think the real issue is that when `overall = "Overall"` is set, `table1` is treating the overall column as an additional stratum, which means the pvalue function is receiving three groups instead of two. The simplest fix is to modify the pvalue function to only use the first two elements of `x`, ignoring any additional strata that might be passed.
</thinking></div>

beta_a_g <- if (length(a_g_term) && !is.na(a_g_term)) grab_term(tidy_df, a_g_term)[1] else 0\n  beta_c_g <- if (length(c_g_term) && !is.na(c_g_term)) grab_term(tidy_df, c_g_term)[1] else 0\n\n  if (any(is.na(c(beta_a, beta_c)))) return(c(NA_real_, NA_real_, NA_real_))\n\n  A   <- beta_a + ifelse(group == \"base\", 0, beta_a_g)\n  C   <- beta_c + ifelse(group == \"base\", 0, beta_c_g)\n  val <- -(A / C) * scaler\n\n  terms <- c(attr, cost_name,\n             if (group != \"base\" && !is.na(a_g_term)) a_g_term else NULL,\n             if (group != \"base\" && !is.na(c_g_term)) c_g_term else NULL)\n  terms <- terms[!is.na(terms) & nzchar(terms)]\n  if (is.null(V) || !all(terms %in% rownames(V))) return(c(val, NA_real_, NA_real_))\n\n  grad <- numeric(length(terms))\n  grad[terms == attr]      <- -1 / C * scaler\n  grad[terms == cost_name] <- (A / C^2) * scaler\n  if (group != \"base\") {\n    if (any(terms == a_g_term)) grad[terms == a_g_term] <- -1 / C * scaler\n    if (any(terms == c_g_term)) grad[terms == c_g_term] <- (A / C^2) * scaler\n  }\n\n  Vsub <- V[terms, terms, drop = FALSE]\n  var  <- as.numeric(t(grad) %*% Vsub %*% grad)\n  if (!is.finite(var) || var < 0) return(c(val, NA_real_, NA_real_))\n  se   <- sqrt(var)\n  pval <- 2 * pnorm(-abs(val / se))\n  c(val, se, pval)\n}\n\ncompute_bic <- function(model) {\n  ll <- as.numeric(logLik(model))\n  k  <- attr(logLik(model), \"df\")\n  n  <- tryCatch(model$n$obs, error = function(e) NA)\n  if (is.na(n)) return(NA_real_)\n  k * log(n) - 2 * ll\n}\n\nlr_bits <- function(model) {\n  ll  <- as.numeric(logLik(model))\n  ll0 <- tryCatch(model$nullLogLik, error = function(e) NA_real_)\n  k   <- attr(logLik(model), \"df\")\n  if (is.na(ll0)) return(list(lr = NA_real_, p = NA_real_, k = k))\n  lr  <- -2 * (ll0 - ll)\n  list(lr = lr, p = pchisq(lr, df = k, lower.tail = FALSE), k = k)\n}\n\n# Build texreg object pair for one model ----\nbuild_pair <- function(model, scaler, cost_name) {\n  tdf <- broom::tidy(model)\n  V   <- tryCatch(vcov(model), error = function(e) NULL)\n\n  coef_vals <- setNames(rep(NA_real_, length(coef_rows)), coef_rows)\n  se_vals   <- coef_vals;  p_vals    <- coef_vals\n  mwtp_vals <- coef_vals;  mwtp_se   <- coef_vals;  mwtp_p <- coef_vals\n\n  for (term in coef_rows) {\n    x <- grab_term(tdf, term)\n    coef_vals[term] <- x[1]; se_vals[term] <- x[2]; p_vals[term] <- x[3]\n  }\n\n  for (term in coef_rows) {\n    g <- term_group(term)\n    if (g %in% c(\"price\", \"price_inter\", \"other\")) next\n    a   <- term_attr(term)\n    out <- mwtp_for_attr_group(a, ifelse(g == \"base\", \"base\", g), tdf, V, scaler, cost_name)\n    mwtp_vals[term] <- out[1]; mwtp_se[term] <- out[2]; mwtp_p[term] <- out[3]\n  }\n\n  ll  <- as.numeric(logLik(model))\n  ll0 <- tryCatch(model$nullLogLik, error = function(e) NA_real_)\n  lr  <- lr_bits(model)\n  gof_n <- c(\"Num. obs.\", \"Log Likelihood\", \"AIC\", \"BIC\", \"McFadden R\\u00b2\",\n             paste0(\"LR \\u03c7\\u00b2 (df=\", lr$k, \")\"), \"p-value (LR)\")\n  gof_v <- c(tryCatch(model$n$obs, error = function(e) NA_integer_),\n             ll, AIC(model), compute_bic(model),\n             if (!is.na(ll0)) 1 - ll / ll0 else NA_real_,\n             lr$lr, lr$p)\n  gof_d <- c(FALSE, TRUE, TRUE, TRUE, TRUE, TRUE, TRUE)\n\n  m_coef <- createTexreg(\n    coef.names  = pretty_labels,\n    coef        = as.numeric(coef_vals),\n    se          = as.numeric(se_vals),\n    pvalues     = as.numeric(p_vals),\n    gof.names   = gof_n,\n    gof         = gof_v,\n    gof.decimal = gof_d\n  )\n\n  m_mwtp <- createTexreg(\n    coef.names = pretty_labels,\n    coef       = as.numeric(mwtp_vals),\n    se         = as.numeric(mwtp_se),\n    pvalues    = as.numeric(mwtp_p)\n  )\n\n  list(m_coef = m_coef, m_mwtp = m_mwtp)\n}\n\n# Build and render ----\nown  <- build_pair(mxl_own,  scaler, cost_name)\nrent <- build_pair(mxl_rent, scaler, cost_name)\n\nhtmlreg(\n  list(own$m_coef, own$m_mwtp, rent$m_coef, rent$m_mwtp),\n  custom.header      = list(\"Owners\" = 1:2, \"Renters\" = 3:4),\n  custom.model.names = c(\"Coef.\", \"MWTP\", \"Coef.\", \"MWTP\"),\n  custom.coef.names  = pretty_labels,\n  digits             = 2,\n  stars              = c(0.001, 0.01, 0.05),\n  na.replace         = \"\\u2013\",\n  caption            = \"Table 5. Interaction regression with age (Old = age \\u226572, i.e. above median; reference: younger)\",\n  caption.above      = TRUE,\n  file               = here(\"output/tables\", \"table_05_interaction_age.html\")\n)\n\nmessage(\"Table 5 saved to output/tables/table_05_interaction_age.html\")\n"}}</script></tool-call></div>

In the interaction tables (tables 5, 6, 7), the `mwtp_for_attr_group` function computes:

```
val <- -(A / C) * scaler
```

where:
- `A = beta_a + beta_a_g` (base attribute coefficient + interaction term coefficient)


- `C = beta_c + beta_c_g` (base price coefficient + price interaction coefficient)
- `scaler = 0.10 * 10500` = 1050

This gives the MWTP for the group defined by the interaction dummy (e.g., "Old" group) as the ratio of effective coefficients times the scaler. In `baseline_regs.R`, the approach is similar but uses a different scaler value of 0.10 * 10000 instead.

Looking at how the scaler works: since price_num is expressed as a fraction ranging from -0.20 to +0.20, a unit change represents a 100% swing in housing costs, so a 10% change equals 0.10 times the median cost. The MWTP formula gives us the marginal rate of substitution in price_num units, and to convert that to SEK I multiply by the scaler—so for a 10% cost change, that's 0.10 times the median monthly cost.

The baseline values make sense: green space 500m away is worth about 397 SEK/month for owners, meaning they'd accept roughly 4% higher housing costs to have it nearby rather than 15km away. But I'm noticing the scaler should actually differ between owners and renters based on their respective median costs—1000 SEK for owners and 900 SEK for renters—rather than using 1050 for both. The interaction terms might also need a different interpretation than I'm currently applying.

Here's what's happening. Let me explain the formula then flag the two issues:

**Current formula (in all interaction table scripts):**
- Base rows: `MWTP = −(β_attr / β_price) × scaler` — the MWTP for the **reference group** (e.g. younger people)
- `× Old` rows: `MWTP = −((β_attr + β_attr_Old) / (β_price + β_price_Old)) × scaler` — the **total** MWTP for the old group, not the marginal difference

**Issue 1 — Scaler:** The interaction tables currently use a single scaler of `0.10 × 10500 = 1050` for both owners and renters. The baseline table (Table 4) uses `0.10 × 10000 = 1000` for owners and `0.10 × 9000 = 900` for renters. That's why the numbers look different.

**Issue 2 — The LaTeX tables don't match either set:** The previously generated `mxl_age_inter.tex` shows owner MWTP = 347, which corresponds to `MRS_owner × 900` — the renter scaler applied to the owner model. That looks like a bug in the original script (the scalers were applied to the wrong models).

Two questions before I fix this:

1. **Scaler:** Should the interaction tables use the same separate scalers as the baseline (1000 for owners, 900 for renters)?

2. **Interaction rows:** Should the `× Old` rows show the **total** MWTP for old people (current approach), or the **difference** — i.e. how much more/less old people are willing to pay compared to the reference group?

<div><thinking id="thinking-1774869056114-j4gii">
The user wants to create a new script that looks at interactions between the price coefficient and various demographic variables (age, sex, health, etc.). They think the approach might be flawed because the coefficients won't be interpretable, but they want to do it anyway for the reviewer.

Let me think about what this means in the context of a mixed logit DCE model.

The reviewer wants to see a "grid" of interactions with the price coefficient. What this likely means is:

In a standard mixed logit, you have:
U = β_attr * attr + β_price * price + ...

The reviewer wants to see models where price is interacted with demographic variables:


U = β_attr * attr + β_price * price + β_price_old * price * Old + ...

So the idea is that β_price_old would capture whether older people are more or less price-sensitive, which then feeds into the MWTP calculations. The concern about interpretability stems from a fundamental issue in random utility models: the scale parameter affecting price sensitivity isn't separately identified from preference heterogeneity, and interacting price with demographics in a mixed logit conflates these two sources of variation in problematic ways.

But actually, looking at the structure here—price is fixed while attributes are random—so the interaction is more straightforward than I initially thought. And checking the existing tables, this is already being done: tables 5, 6, and 7 already include price interactions with demographics like `price_Old`. The reviewer might be asking for something more targeted though: models where only price is interacted with demographics (age, sex, health status) rather than all attributes, to isolate how price sensitivity differs across groups and present those coefficients with their significance levels.

The user's concern about interpretability makes sense—there could be identification issues or sign/scale problems with price interactions in mixed logit. So I'm weighing three approaches: estimating separate models for each demographic subgroup to compare price coefficients directly, adding only price×demographic interactions to the baseline, or recognizing that the current interaction models already capture this. The real question is which approach would give the most interpretable and defensible results.

Looking back at what the user actually asked for—a grid showing how respondents price characteristics across subgroups—I think they want a structured table with attributes as rows and demographic categories as columns, displaying the marginal willingness to pay for each combination. Since the interaction models are already estimated and saved, I should extract the price coefficients from those models and compute the effective MWTP for each subgroup, then organize everything into that grid format. I see the tension here—they want to isolate price sensitivity differences across demographics, but they're worried the coefficients won't be interpretable. They're asking me to recommend the best approach for a new script that explores price interactions specifically. Let me think through what would actually work: a model with price interacted only with demographics (not all attributes) would show whether willingness to pay for the good itself varies by group, which is cleaner than the current all-interactions approach and more directly answers the reviewer's concern. (most defensible)**: Use the MWTP estimates from the existing interaction models to create a comparison grid. This doesn't require new models and uses the full interaction specification.

**Option 2 (what reviewer asked for)**: Estimate price-only interaction models where only `price × demographic` is added to the base model. This specifically isolates price sensitivity.

**Option 3 (simplest)**: Just estimate separate subgroup models (e.g., separate MXL for Old vs Young) and compare price coefficients directly.

I should note the interpretability concern and suggest Option 1 as the most defensible, while also providing Option 2 if the reviewer specifically wants price interactions.

Let me write the plan.

For the plan:
- New script: `scripts/paper/tables/table_reviewer_price_interactions.R`
- Approach: Two parts:
  1. Extract MWTP from existing interaction models (already estimated) and present as a comparison grid showing rows for attributes and columns for subgroup pairs
  2. Note that the interaction terms in the existing models already capture `price × demographic` effects, so the MWTP comparison directly reveals how different groups value each characteristic

The output would be a flextable with attributes as rows and demographic subgroups as columns, displaying MWTP values for each combination. This approach is interpretable, leverages existing models, and directly answers what the reviewer is asking about how much different respondents value various characteristics. I'll format the output as a flextable to make the comparison grid clean and readable. The MWTP values themselves are fully interpretable since they reflect the combined effect of preference and price sensitivity differences across subgroups, which directly addresses the reviewer's concern—and since the existing models already include the necessary price interactions, I don't need to estimate anything new.

<div><tool-call id="toolu_01FxasGnGazQ3H4P6d2k2LWA"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"name":"write","input":{"file_path":"C:/Users/ni3054ch/.positai/plans/2026-03-30-1055-plan.md","content":"# Plan: Reviewer — Price Interaction Grid\n**Date:** 2026-03-30\n\n---\n\n## Reviewer's Request...[truncated, total 3994 chars]"},"caption":"C:/Users/ni3054ch/.positai/plans/2026-03-30-1055-plan.md","inputPreview":{"type":"code","value":"# Plan: Reviewer — Price Interaction Grid\n**Date:** 2026-03-30\n\n---\n\n## Reviewer's Request\n\nShow how the *price coefficient* interacts with demographic variables (age, sex, health) to reveal how much different groups \"price\" DCE attributes. The output should be a grid.\n\n---\n\n## The Interpretability Problem (and the Solution)\n\nThe reviewer's underlying question — \"do different groups have different price sensitivities / WTP?\" — is entirely valid and answerable. The concern is that **presenting the raw `price × demographic` interaction coefficient alone** is not directly interpretable, because:\n\n- The coefficient gives the *change* in price sensitivity for the interaction group, on the utility scale\n- It cannot be read as a \"willingness to pay\" number without combining it with the base price coefficient and the attribute coefficients\n- In a correlated mixed logit, the price coefficient also has a distributional component\n\n**The best answer to the reviewer is the MWTP grid.** The existing interaction models (`mxl_old_owner/renter`, `mxl_sex_owner/renter`, `mxl_health_own/rent`) already include `price × demographic` interaction terms *alongside* all attribute interactions. The MWTP derived from these models **does** capture differential price sensitivity — it is computed as:\n\n- Reference group: `−(β_attr / β_price) × scaler`\n- Interaction group: `−((β_attr + β_attr_D) / (β_price + β_price_D)) × scaler`\n\nThis is exactly what the reviewer wants: a number that reflects how much each group values each attribute in monetary terms, already accounting for their price sensitivity.\n\n---\n\n## New Script\n\n**`scripts/paper/tables/table_reviewer_mwtp_grid.R`**\n\nOutput: `output/tables/table_reviewer_mwtp_grid.html`\n\n### What it produces\n\nA single wide comparison table with this structure:\n\n| Attribute | Owners: Younger | Owners: Old (≥72) | Owners: Women | Owners: Men | Owners: Not v. good health | Owners: Very good health |\n|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|\n| Green space: 5 km | XXX | XXX | XXX | XXX | XXX | XXX |\n| ... | | | | | | |\n\nAnd a second panel below (or separate table) for **Renters** with the same columns.\n\nMWTP values are in SEK/month, rounded to integers. A note accompanies the table explaining that values account for both attribute preference heterogeneity and price sensitivity heterogeneity.\n\n### Models used (all pre-saved, no re-estimation)\n\n| Interaction | Owner model | Renter model | Groups shown |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| Age | `mxl_old_owner.rds` | `mxl_old_renter.rds` | Younger / Old (≥72) |\n| Sex | `mxl_sex_owner.rds` | `mxl_sex_renter.rds` | Women / Men |\n| Health | `mxl_health_own.rds` | `mxl_health_rent.rds` | Not very good / Very good |\n\n### How MWTP is extracted\n\nThe `mwtp_for_attr_group()` function from the interaction table scripts is reused. For each attribute × group combination:\n\n```\nmwtp_ref   = −(β_attr / β_price) × scaler\nmwtp_inter = −((β_attr + β_attr_D) / (β_price + β_price_D)) × scaler\n```\n\nScalers: owners = 1000, renters = 900 (consistent with Tables 4–7).\n\n### Caveats included in table note\n\n- MWTP values combine attribute preference heterogeneity *and* price sensitivity heterogeneity — the `price × D` term contributes to both the numerator change (if the attribute interaction exists) and the denominator\n- Standard errors / significance of MWTP *differences between groups* are not shown; for that, the interaction coefficient p-values in Tables 5–7 are the relevant test\n- The grid is descriptive; inferential interpretation of group differences should rely on the interaction coefficient significance in Tables 5–7\n\n---\n\n## What this does NOT do\n\n- Does NOT estimate new models\n- Does NOT show raw `price × demographic` coefficients in isolation (these are not interpretable on their own)\n- Does NOT imply the differences in MWTP are statistically significant (that's what Tables 5–7 are for)\n\n---\n\n## File to create\n\n```\nscripts/paper/tables/table_reviewer_mwtp_grid.R\noutput/tables/table_reviewer_mwtp_grid.html\n```\n"}}</script></tool-call></div>

The reviewer wants to interact the price coefficient with the attributes - meaning they want to estimate a model where `price × attribute` interaction terms are included. This is different from what we've been doing.

So the model would look like:
U = β_attr * attr + β_price * price + β_price_green5km * (price × green5km) + β_price_green500m * (price × green500m) + ...

The idea is: does the price people pay affect how they value specific attributes? Or conversely, does the attribute level affect price sensitivity?

But as the user notes, this is econometrically flawed in a DCE context. Here's why:


In a DCE, attributes are designed to be orthogonal to each other, so interacting price with other attributes doesn't make conceptual sense - you're essentially asking whether the value of green space varies by price level when the whole point of the design is that they're independent. And in a logit model, adding a price × attribute interaction doesn't really estimate something fundamentally different; it just changes how the price coefficient varies with attribute levels, which makes the MWTP calculation much harder to interpret. The MWTP approach is actually the right way to capture how people trade off attributes against price.

The reviewer might be conflating this with standard regression where you'd interact price with outcomes, but in a DCE framework, the MWTP already does that work. What they probably actually want is either a clearer presentation of the MWTP table, a side-by-side visualization of MWTP across attributes, or possibly the marginal rate of substitution to show relative valuations without converting to monetary terms. I should help the user explain why the interaction approach doesn't work here and suggest presenting the MWTP results more clearly as the answer to what the reviewer is really asking for. note clearly why this is not the standard approach
2. Show how MWTP is actually the correct way to address their question

Let me think about what "price × attribute" interaction means in this context:

Model: U = Σ β_i * x_i + β_p * price + Σ β_ip * (price * x_i) + ε

Where β_ip captures the "interaction" between price and attribute i.

This would estimate how the marginal utility of price changes depending on which attribute level is present. This is unusual and potentially identified from correlations in the data.

Actually, this model doesn't make much conceptual sense in a DCE where attributes are orthogonally designed. The price × attribute interaction would require that the data contains variation in price at each attribute level combination, which it does have (since the design includes all combinations), but the interpretation is unclear.

A common alternative that reviewers sometimes confuse with this is **separate price coefficients by attribute** - which also doesn't quite work. What would actually make sense is either a random coefficient model where price sensitivity varies across respondents, or a visualization showing how utility changes across different price and attribute combinations. Understood — the reviewer wants to add `price × attribute` interaction terms to the utility function (e.g. `price × dist_green5km`, `price × shops500m`, etc.) to see if price sensitivity varies across attribute levels. You're right that this is a conceptually odd request in a DCE context, because the MWTP ratio already captures exactly that — it is the price coefficient relative to each attribute coefficient. Let me think through this clearly before writing anything:

**What the reviewer is asking for:**  
A model of the form `U = β_a·attr + β_p·price + β_pa·(price × attr) + ...` — testing whether the marginal disutility of price changes depending on which attribute level is in the choice scenario.

**Why it's problematic:**
- In a well-designed DCE, price and attributes are orthogonal by construction, so these interactions are identified only from individual-level heterogeneity in the panel
- The `β_pa` coefficient has no clean interpretation: it doesn't tell you "how much people value attribute A" — that's exactly what `−β_a / β_p` (i.e. MWTP) already answers
- In the MXL with correlated random parameters, the covariance between attribute and price coefficients already captures this heterogeneity structurally

**The best response to the reviewer:**  
Show them Table 4 (the MWTP table) is precisely the answer to their question, framed clearly. MWTP = `−β_a / β_p` *is* the price-attribute interaction — it is the rate at which one can substitute money for attribute A. A nicely formatted MWTP comparison across attributes, perhaps with a short explanatory note, is more informative than raw price × attribute coefficients.

1. Estimates the price × attribute interaction model as requested (owners and renters separately), saves the models
2. Presents the coefficients in a table with a clear note about limited interpretability
3. Alongside it, shows the MWTP table as the proper framing — so you have both outputs ready and can decide which to include / how to respond

Does that sound right, or would you prefer one or the other?

\"p_space\")\n\nif (!file.exists(path_own)) {\n  message(\"Estimating owner model with price × attribute interactions …\")\n  set.seed(7341)\n  mxl_price_attr_own <- logitr(\n    data           = {\n  mxl_price_attr_rent <- readRDS(path_rent)\n  message(\"Renter model loaded from disk.\")\n}\n\n# ── 3. Extract coefficients ───────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\ntdf_own  <- broom::tidy(mxl_price_attr_own)  |> filter(!str_starts(term, \"sd_\"))\ntdf_rent <- broom::tidy(mxl_price_attr_rent) |> filter(!str_starts(term, \"sd_\"))\n\nsig_stars <- function(p) {\n  case_when(\n    is.na(p)  ~ \"\",\n    p < 0.001 ~ \"***\",\n    p < 0.01  ~ \"**\",\n    p < 0.05  ~ \"*\",\n    TRUE      ~ \"\"\n  )\n}\n\nfmt_coef <- function(est, se, p) {\n  if (is.na(est)) return(\"–\")\n  paste0(sprintf(\"%.2f\", est), sig_stars(p), \"\\n(\", sprintf(\"%.2f\", se), \")\")\n}\n\n# ── 4. Build grid table (A): price × attribute interaction coefficients ────────\n\n# Attribute row labels and the corresponding price-interaction term name\ninter_map <- tribble(\n  ~label,                              ~term,\n  \"Green space: 5 km (vs 15 km)\",      \"p_green5km\",\n  \"Green space: 500 m (vs 15 km)\",     \"p_green500m\",\n  \"Shops: 5 km (vs 15 km)\",            \"p_shops5km\",\n  \"Shops: 500 m (vs 15 km)\",           \"p_shops500m\",\n  \"Transit stop: 600 m (vs 900 m)\",    \"p_trans600\",\n  \"Transit stop: 300 m (vs 900 m)\",    \"p_trans300\",\n  \"Parking: reserved garage (vs none)\",\"p_garage\",\n  \"Parking: reserved space (vs none)\", \"p_space\"\n)\n\n# Also pull the baseline price coefficient row\nprice_row <- tibble(\n  label = \"Price (baseline)\",\n  term  = \"price_num\"\n)\n\nall_rows <- bind_rows(price_row, inter_map)\n\ngrid_df <- all_rows |>\n  rowwise() |>\n  mutate(\n    own_row  = tdf_own[tdf_own$term  == term, , drop = FALSE],\n    rent_row = tdf_rent[tdf_rent$term == term, , drop = FALSE],\n    Owner  = fmt_coef(\n      if (nrow(own_row)  > 0) own_row$estimate[1]  else NA_real_,\n      if (nrow(own_row)  > 0) own_row$std.error[1] else NA_real_,\n      if (nrow(own_row)  > 0) own_row$p.value[1]   else NA_real_\n    ),\n    Renter = fmt_coef(\n      if (nrow(rent_row) > 0) rent_row$estimate[1]  else NA_real_,\n      if (nrow(rent_row) > 0) rent_row$std.error[1] else NA_real_,\n      if (nrow(rent_row) > 0) rent_row$p.value[1]   else NA_real_\n    )\n  ) |>\n  ungroup() |>\n  select(Attribute = label, Owner, Renter)\n\nft_grid <- flextable(grid_df) |>\n  add_header_row(values = c(\"\", \"Owners\", \"Renters\"), colwidths = c(1, 1, 1)) |>\n  bold(part = \"header\") |>\n  align(j = 2:3, align = \"center\") |>\n  align(j = 2:3, align = \"center\", part = \"header\") |>\n  # Shade the baseline price row to distinguish it from interaction rows\n  bg(i = 1, bg = \"#f2f2f2\") |>\n  autofit() |>\n  theme_booktabs() |>\n  add_footer_lines(\n    \"Coefficients from mixed logit with correlated random parameters and price \\u00d7 attribute\ninteraction terms. Standard errors in parentheses. Significance: * p<0.05, ** p<0.01, *** p<0.001.\n\nIMPORTANT: The price \\u00d7 attribute interaction coefficient shows how the marginal\ndisutility of price changes in the presence of each attribute level. These coefficients\nare not directly interpretable as willingness to pay. See the MWTP table below for\nthe monetised valuation of each attribute.\"\n  ) |>\n  set_caption(caption = \"Price \\u00d7 attribute interaction coefficients — owners and renters\")\n\nsave_as_html(ft_grid,\n             path = here(\"output/tables\", \"table_reviewer_price_attr_coefs.html\"))\nmessage(\"Grid table saved to output/tables/table_reviewer_price_attr_coefs.html\")\n\n# ── 5. Build MWTP table (B): the interpretable counterpart ───────────────────\n\nscaler_own  <- 0.10 * 10000\nscaler_rent <- 0.10 * 9000\ncost_name   <- \"price_num\"\n\ncompute_mwtp <- function(tdf, scaler) {\n  beta_p <- tdf$estimate[tdf$term == cost_name]\n  V      <- tryCatch(vcov(mxl_price_attr_own), error = function(e) NULL)\n\n  inter_map |>\n    rowwise() |>\n    mutate(\n      attr_term   = str_remove(term, \"^p_\"),   # e.g. p_green5km → green5km\n      beta_a      = { r <- tdf[tdf$term == attr_term, ]; if (nrow(r) > 0) r$estimate[1] else NA_real_ },\n      beta_pa     = { r <- tdf[tdf$term == term,       ]; if (nrow(r) > 0) r$estimate[1] else NA_real_ },\n      mwtp        = if (!is.na(beta_a)) round(-(beta_a / beta_p) * scaler) else NA_integer_\n    ) |>\n    ungroup() |>\n    select(label, mwtp)\n}\n\nmwtp_own_new  <- compute_mwtp(tdf_own,  scaler_own)\nmwtp_rent_new <- compute_mwtp(tdf_rent, scaler_rent)\n\n# Load baseline MWTP for comparison (from Table 4)\nmxl_own_base  <- readRDS(here(\"output/models\", \"mxl_owner_base.rds\"))\nmxl_rent_base <- readRDS(here(\"output/models\", \"mxl_renter_base.rds\"))\n\ntdf_own_base  <- broom::tidy(mxl_own_base)  |> filter(!str_starts(term, \"sd_\"))\ntdf_rent_base <- broom::tidy(mxl_rent_base) |> filter(!str_starts(term, \"sd_\"))\n\nbase_attr_map <- c(\n  \"p_green5km\"  = \"dist_green5km\",\n  \"p_green500m\" = \"dist_green500m\",\n  \"p_shops5km\"  = \"dist_shops5km\",\n  \"p_shops500m\" = \"dist_shops500m\",\n  \"p_trans600\"  = \"dist_trans600\",\n  \"p_trans300\"  = \"dist_trans300\",\n  \"p_garage\"    = \"park_garage\",\n  \"p_space\"     = \"park_space\"\n)\n\nmwtp_base <- inter_map |>\n  rowwise() |>\n  mutate(\n    base_term  = base_attr_map[[term]],\n    beta_a_own  = { r <- tdf_own_base[tdf_own_base$term  == base_term, ]; if (nrow(r) > 0) r$estimate[1] else NA_real_ },\n    beta_p_own  = tdf_own_base$estimate[tdf_own_base$term  == cost_name],\n    beta_a_rent = { r <- tdf_rent_base[tdf_rent_base$term == base_term, ]; if (nrow(r) > 0) r$estimate[1] else NA_real_ },\n    beta_p_rent = tdf_rent_base$estimate[tdf_rent_base$term == cost_name],\n    mwtp_own_base  = round(-(beta_a_own  / beta_p_own)  * scaler_own),\n    mwtp_rent_base = round(-(beta_a_rent / beta_p_rent) * scaler_rent)\n  ) |>\n  ungroup()\n\nmwtp_compare <- tibble(\n  Attribute             = inter_map$label,\n  `Owner (interaction model)`  = mwtp_own_new$mwtp,\n  `Owner (baseline)`           = mwtp_base$mwtp_own_base,\n  `Renter (interaction model)` = mwtp_rent_new$mwtp,\n  `Renter (baseline)`          = mwtp_base$mwtp_rent_base\n)\n\nft_mwtp <- flextable(mwtp_compare) |>\n  add_header_row(\n    values     = c(\"\", \"Owners\", \"Renters\"),\n    colwidths  = c(1, 2, 2)\n  ) |>\n  bold(part = \"header\") |>\n  align(j = 2:5, align = \"center\") |>\n  align(j = 2:5, align = \"center\", part = \"header\") |>\n  colformat_int(j = 2:5) |>\n  autofit() |>\n  theme_booktabs() |>\n  add_footer_lines(\n    \"MWTP in SEK/month (10% of median monthly housing cost: owners 10,000 SEK, renters 9,000 SEK).\nInteraction model: mixed logit with price \\u00d7 attribute terms.\nBaseline model: standard mixed logit (Table 4 of the paper).\nMWTP = \\u2212(\\u03b2_attribute / \\u03b2_price) \\u00d7 scaler. This is the correct monetary\nexpression of how much each group values each attribute.\"\n  ) |>\n  set_caption(caption = \"MWTP comparison: interaction model vs baseline (SEK/month)\")\n\nsave_as_html(ft_mwtp,\n             path = here(\"output/tables\", \"table_reviewer_price_attr_mwtp.html\"))\nmessage(\"MWTP comparison table saved to output/tables/table_reviewer_price_attr_mwtp.html\")\n"}}</script></tool-call></div>

Both tables are clean. A couple of things worth noting from the output:

**The MWTP comparison is telling.** Most values from the interaction model track closely with the baseline (e.g. shops 500m owner: 596 vs 598; parking garage owner: 615 vs 587). The main exceptions are green space 5km owner (77 vs 200) and renter (55 vs 214) — suggesting the price × green5km interaction is absorbing some of the green space effect, which is a sign of the interpretability problem you anticipated.

**The coefficient grid** shows mostly non-significant price × attribute interactions (few stars), consistent with the orthogonal design. The few significant ones (transit for renters, green500m for renters) are likely noise at 20 draws.

Both files are in `output/tables/`. The grid is the reviewer's requested output; the MWTP table is there to accompany it with a note explaining it's the more interpretable framing.

Let me rewrite just the new portion about interaction terms and challenges:

The interaction terms like `p_green5km` test whether price sensitivity shifts depending on green space proximity—a positive coefficient would mean price becomes less disutilizing when green is 5km away, though this gets confounded with the scale parameter. The core challenge is that price isn't on an absolute monetary scale, so a 10% change means different things for owners versus renters, and comparing MWTP across groups requires accounting for the scale adjustment. Similarly, the categorical coefficients live on the utility scale and aren't directly comparable in magnitude, and while the interactions specifically examine whether price sensitivity varies by attribute level, the baseline model already captures some of this variation.

Now for the Quarto document. Here's the proposed outline before I write it:

**`docs/reviewer_note_price_interactions.qmd`**

1. **Overview** — purpose of this note; the reviewer's request and why it raises methodological questions

2. **Model specification** — the utility function written out formally, distinguishing the baseline MXL from the price×attribute variant; what each term does

3. **Attribute coding and reference levels**
   - All attributes are dummy-coded; what the reference levels are (15 km green/shops, 900 m transit, no parking)
   - How this means each coefficient is *relative to its reference*, not an absolute value
   - Why you can't directly compare a green-space coefficient to a transit coefficient

4. **Price coding** — the key interpretive challenge
   - `price_num = raw_price / 100`, where raw_price ∈ {−20, 0, +20}
   - So `price_num` ∈ {−0.2, 0, 0.2}: not on a money scale, but a *fraction of planned monthly cost*
   - A "unit change" in price_num = a 100% change in cost — not meaningful
   - MWTP scaler (0.10 × median cost) converts to "SEK per 10% cost change"
   - Consequence: raw price coefficients are sensitive to the respondent's *planned cost*, not a fixed monetary unit

5. **The price×attribute interaction terms** — what they actually test
   - Each term (e.g. `price_num × green5km`) asks: does price disutility change when green space is 5 km?
   - Interpretation is on the utility scale, not SEK — two layers of indirection from money
   - The MWTP comparison table shows the practical consequence: where interactions are large, the MWTP shifts

6. **Why MWTP is the recommended summary** — normalises by price coefficient, puts all attributes on the same monetary scale, and directly answers "how much is attribute X worth?"

Does this outline work, or would you like to adjust the emphasis or add/remove sections?

## Databot



<div><thinking id="thinking-1774872279160-8ypm7">
The user is asking a conceptual/methodological question about point 5 in the outline: they're pointing out that comparing attribute-level coefficients is hard not just because of the utility scale, but because:

1. The intervals between attribute levels are non-symmetrical within an attribute (e.g., for distance to green space: 15km → 5km is a 10km reduction, but 5km → 500m is a 4.5km reduction — very different physical intervals, both coded as binary dummies)
2. Different attributes have different numbers of levels (some have 3 levels, creating 2 dummies each)


3. Different attributes measure entirely different things (distance, parking type, price %)

So the user is making a really good point: even after accounting for the utility scale, the coefficients for different dummy variables can't be directly compared because they represent fundamentally different physical magnitudes. A 10km improvement in green space proximity isn't comparable to a 14.5km improvement, and neither is directly comparable to changes in parking availability or price. The coefficients are on the same utility scale, but the underlying attribute changes they represent are incommensurable. leading — you can't directly compare a 500m effect to a 5km effect without accounting for the different intervals they represent. MWTP normalizes by price sensitivity but doesn't solve the fundamental non-symmetry problem. The real approach is to frame comparisons around policy-relevant scenarios, like comparing the value of reducing green space from 15km to 500m versus transit from 900m to 300m. I should add this as a dedicated section in the Quarto document, either under attribute coding or as its own point on coefficient non-comparability, then update the outline accordingly.
</thinking></div>

Yes, exactly — and this is actually a more fundamental problem than the utility-scale issue. There are two layers of non-comparability:

**Within an attribute:** The levels are not evenly spaced, so the dummies don't represent equal-sized steps. For green space: `green5km` = going from 15 km to 5 km (a 10 km improvement); `green500m` = going from 15 km to 500 m (a 14.5 km improvement). The second dummy covers nearly 1.5× the physical distance but you can't divide one coefficient by the other and call it a rate. Transit is similar: `trans600` = 300 m closer; `trans300` = 600 m closer — the second level represents twice the physical change.

**Across attributes:** The units are entirely incommensurable. A coefficient on `green5km` reflects a 10 km change in green-space distance. A coefficient on `trans600` reflects a 300 m change in transit proximity. A coefficient on `park_garage` reflects a qualitative step from nothing to a reserved garage. These numbers sit on the same utility scale but represent physically incomparable magnitudes.

**And then price on top:** Not only is price coded as a fraction of planned cost rather than a fixed SEK amount, but the planned cost differs across respondents — so the price coefficient absorbs a distribution of individual planned costs, not a fixed monetary unit.

The consequence is that the `price × attribute` interaction coefficients the reviewer wanted are doubly hard to compare: the price variable is on one non-intuitive scale, and each attribute dummy represents a physically different-sized intervention. MWTP at least collapses this to a single monetary dimension, though it still doesn't resolve the "5 km green space vs 500 m" comparison — for that you'd need to decide on a specific counterfactual (e.g. "value of moving from 15 km to 500 m") and use the appropriate dummy.

I'll add this as its own section in the document. Let me update the plan:

Overview\nBrief statement of purpose: what the reviewer requested, and why this note exists. Flags that the price×attribute interaction approach raises non-trivial interpretive challenges addressed in the sections below.\n\n---\n\n### 2. Model specification\nWrite out the utility function formally for both the baseline MXL and the price×attribute variant:\n\n- **Baseline:** `U = Σ β_a · attr_a + β_p · price_num + ε`\n- **Price×attr:** `U = Σ β_a · attr_a + β_p · price_num + Σ β_pa · (price_num × attr_a) + ε`\n\nExplain what `β_pa` adds: it estimates whether price sensitivity shifts in the presence of a particular attribute level.\n\n---\n\n### 3. Attribute coding and reference levels\n\n- All attributes are **dummy-coded** (binary indicator per non-reference level). The model never \"sees\" the physical magnitude of the level, only whether it is present or absent.\n- Reference levels: 15 km (green space), 15 km (shops), 900 m (transit), no parking, 0% price change.\n- Coefficients are therefore **relative contrasts**, not absolute effects.\n- Parking is qualitative (none / reserved space / reserved garage) — the levels have no natural metric spacing at all.\n\n---\n\n### 4. The non-symmetrical interval problem (within and across attributes)\n\nThis section directly addresses the reviewer's implicit assumption that coefficients are comparable.\n\n**Within an attribute — unequal intervals:**\n\n| Attribute | Level 1 dummy | Physical change from reference | Level 2 dummy | Physical change from reference |\n|---|---|---|---|---|\n| Green space | 5 km | −10 km | 500 m | −14.5 km |\n| Shops | 5 km | −10 km | 500 m | −14.5 km |\n| Transit | 600 m | −300 m | 300 m | −600 m |\n| Parking | Reserved space | qualitative | Reserved garage | qualitative |\n\nBecause each dummy is 0/1, both dummies within an attribute have the same \"size\" on the variable scale, even though they represent very different physical magnitudes. `β_green500m / β_green5km` is not the \"marginal utility per km of green space\" — it is the contrast between 500 m and 15 km vs the contrast between 5 km and 15 km. These are not divisible in a meaningful way.\n\n**Across attributes — incommensurable units:**\n\nComparing `β_green5km` (reflects a 10 km proximity change) to `β_trans600` (reflects a 300 m proximity change) to `β_park_garage` (reflects a qualitative step) is fundamentally not meaningful on the coefficient scale alone. All three numbers sit on the same utility axis, but the physical interventions they represent are incomparable.\n\n**Consequence for the price×attribute interaction table:**\n\nThe reviewer's grid of `price × attr` coefficients is subject to both layers of this problem: the price variable is on its own non-intuitive scale, *and* each attribute dummy represents a physically different-sized change. A significant `β_price × green5km` cannot be compared in magnitude to a significant `β_price × trans300` without knowing the physical magnitude difference.\n\n---\n\n### 5. Price coding — the fraction-of-planned-cost problem\n\n- `price_num = raw_price / 100`, where raw_price ∈ {−20, 0, +20}.\n- So `price_num` ∈ {−0.2, 0, 0.2}: it is a *fraction of planned monthly housing cost*, not a fixed SEK amount.\n- A \"one unit\" change in `price_num` would represent a 100% cost increase — meaningless as a reference point.\n- The relevant variation in the data is from −0.2 to +0.2 (a 0.4-unit range).\n- **Individual heterogeneity:** planned costs differ across respondents (median ~10,000 SEK for owners, ~9,000 for renters), so the price coefficient absorbs a distribution of individual planned costs — it is not anchored to a fixed monetary unit.\n- **Consequence for interpretation:** `β_price = −5` means \"a unit decrease in price_num increases utility by 5\", which translates to \"a 10% cost decrease (0.1 units) increases utility by 0.5\" — only meaningful after applying the scaler.\n- The MWTP scaler `0.10 × median_cost` converts this to SEK/month for a 10% cost change. This is a convention, not an absolute.\n\n---\n\n### 6. The price×attribute interaction terms — what they actually test\n\n- `p_green5km = price_num × green5km_dummy`: takes the value `price_num` when the green space level is 5 km, and 0 otherwise.\n- `β_p_green5km > 0` means: when green space is at 5 km (vs 15 km reference), the disutility of a price increase is *reduced*. Equivalently, respondents are more willing to pay a price premium when green space is nearby.\n- **But:** the magnitude of `β_p_green5km` is on the same doubly-indirected scale: it is utility per unit of price_num per presence of the 5 km dummy. Converting to an interpretable quantity requires computing MWTP (which accounts for both the attribute and price effects jointly).\n- This is why the MWTP comparison table (showing how MWTP shifts in the interaction model vs baseline) is the most useful summary of these terms.\n\n---\n\n### 7. MWTP as the recommended summary\n\n- MWTP = `−β_a / β_p × scaler` collapses the attribute and price coefficients into a single monetary metric.\n- It expresses: \"how many SEK/month would a respondent accept as a cost increase in exchange for the attribute improvement?\"\n- This resolves the price-scale problem (normalises by `β_p`) but does **not** resolve the non-symmetrical interval problem: MWTP for \"green space 5 km vs 15 km\" and \"green space 500 m vs 15 km\" are still comparing different physical magnitudes.\n- Proper policy comparison requires choosing the counterfactual explicitly (e.g., \"value of moving from 15 km to 500 m\" = `β_green500m / β_p × scaler`; this is the single-step contrast, not a per-km figure).\n- Present the MWTP comparison table (baseline vs interaction model) with commentary.\n\n---\n\n### 8. Summary and recommendation for reviewer response\n\n- The price×attribute coefficient grid is shown as requested.\n- Recommend the reviewer treat it as a **specification check** (do the main results change when price×attribute interactions are added?) rather than a primary result.\n- The answer is: MWTP estimates are broadly stable for most attributes (differences < 50 SEK/month), with the exception of green space (especially for renters), suggesting some collinearity between the green space and price terms in the renter sample.\n- The baseline model (Tables 3–4 of the paper) remains the preferred specification.\n\n---\n\n## Technical notes\n\n- All data and models loaded via `here::here()` — no hardcoded paths.\n- Models `mxl_price_attr_own.rds` and `mxl_price_attr_rent.rds` loaded from `output/models/`.\n- Tables rendered inline using `flextable` with `knitr` output.\n- Document format: HTML output (self-contained), suitable for sharing with the reviewer.\n"}}</script></tool-call></div>

<div><thinking id="thinking-1774873073171-0oxyi">
The user has two questions/points:

1. **Is the price×attr model MWTP interpretable in SEK?** - They're questioning whether the MWTP computed from the interaction model is actually valid/interpretable. Let me think about this:

In the interaction model:
U = β_a * attr + β_p * price + β_pa * (price × attr) + ...

The MWTP for the "interaction" model in the last table was computed as:
MWTP = -(β_a / β_p) × scaler

This is the SAME formula as the baseline model - it ignores the interaction terms. 

So I'm realizing the issue: my MWTP calculation only pulls the main effect coefficients and completely ignores the interaction term, which means it's only valid when the attribute is at its reference level. For a proper interaction model, I'd need to account for how the price coefficient changes depending on the attribute value, but I'm not doing that at all. In the interaction model, the marginal utility of the attribute actually depends on the price level in the choice scenario—it's not constant. This means MWTP isn't a single fixed value but varies across different price points, which breaks the standard MWTP interpretation that assumes a constant ratio. So the user's concern is valid: applying the basic MWTP formula to an interaction model produces a misleading result that doesn't cleanly translate to willingness to pay.

Now I'm thinking through how to handle this in the Quarto document. I should either remove the MWTP comparison table entirely or keep it but add a clear explanation that the interaction model's MWTP column only reflects the main effects and ignores the interaction terms—which means it's not a proper representation of willingness to pay under that specification. I also need to set `echo: false` globally in the YAML to suppress code output.

Actually, I think the cleanest approach is to reframe the table to show only the baseline MWTP and explicitly note that the price×attribute interaction model doesn't produce a straightforward MWTP estimate. This makes the point that the interaction specification is problematic and reinforces why the baseline model is the better choice.

Now I'm updating the Quarto document to suppress code output globally, remove the problematic MWTP table from the interaction model section, and add a clear explanation of why that model doesn't yield interpretable willingness-to-pay estimates.
</thinking></div>

You're right on both counts.

**On the MWTP table:** The interaction model MWTP column is misleading. In the price×attribute model, the marginal utility of an attribute is:

$$\frac{\partial U}{\partial \text{attr}} = \beta_a + \beta_{pa} \cdot \text{price}$$

The price level appears in the numerator — so the MWTP is not a single value, it varies with the price level in the choice scenario. The formula `−β_a / β_p` ignores the interaction term in the numerator entirely, producing numbers that look like MWTP but aren't. That table should go — the honest statement is that **the interaction model doesn't produce a clean MWTP**, which is itself another reason the baseline is preferred.

I'll fix the Quarto doc: remove that table, replace it with a clear explanation of why, and hide all code.
