The reviewer asked to see the price coefficient interacted with each attribute level, expressed as a grid of coefficients.\n\nThis is a legitimate specification to consider, but it raises several interpretive challenges that are important to communicate clearly. This note works through each challenge in turn, and concludes that the MWTP estimates from the baseline model (Tables 3–4 of the paper) remain the most appropriate summary of how respondents value each attribute.\n\n```{r}\n#| label: load-packages\nlibrary(pacman)\np_load(here, broom, logitr, dplyr, tidyr, stringr, flextable, tibble, knitr)\n```\n\n```{r}\n#| label: load-data\nmxl_own_base  <- readRDS(here(\"output/models\", \"mxl_owner_base.rds\"))\nmxl_rent_base <- readRDS(here(\"output/models\", \"mxl_renter_base.rds\"))\nmxl_own_inter  <- readRDS(here(\"output/models\", \"mxl_price_attr_own.rds\"))\nmxl_rent_inter <- readRDS(here(\"output/models\", \"mxl_price_attr_rent.rds\"))\n\ntdf_own_base  <- broom::tidy(mxl_own_base)  |> filter(!str_starts(term, \"sd_\"))\ntdf_rent_base <- broom::tidy(mxl_rent_base) |> filter(!str_starts(term, \"sd_\"))\ntdf_own_inter  <- broom::tidy(mxl_own_inter)  |> filter(!str_starts(term, \"sd_\"))\ntdf_rent_inter <- broom::tidy(mxl_rent_inter) |> filter(!str_starts(term, \"sd_\"))\n```\n\n# Model specification\n\nThe paper uses a mixed logit (MXL) model with correlated random parameters. The baseline utility function for respondent $i$ choosing alternative $j$ in choice occasion $t$ is:\n\n$$\nU_{ijt} = \\sum_{a} \\beta_{ia} \\cdot x_{ajt} + \\beta_p \\cdot \\text{price}_{jt} + \\varepsilon_{ijt}\n$$\n\nwhere $x_{ajt}$ are dummy-coded attribute levels (see Section 3), $\\text{price}_{jt}$ is the price variable (see Section 5), and $\\beta_{ia}$ are individual-level random coefficients drawn from a multivariate normal distribution.\n\nThe **price × attribute interaction model** adds fixed interaction terms:\n\n$$\nU_{ijt} = \\sum_{a} \\beta_{ia} \\cdot x_{ajt} + \\beta_p \\cdot \\text{price}_{jt} + \\sum_{a} \\beta_{pa} \\cdot (\\text{price}_{jt} \\times x_{ajt}) + \\varepsilon_{ijt}\n$$\n\nThe additional term $\\beta_{pa}$ estimates whether the marginal disutility of price changes when a particular attribute level is present. If $\\beta_{pa} > 0$, price is *less* disutilising when that attribute level is in the scenario — equivalently, respondents are more willing to accept a price premium when it accompanies that attribute level.\n\n# Attribute coding and reference levels\n\nAll attributes are **dummy-coded**: for each attribute with $k$ levels, $k - 1$ binary (0/1) indicator variables are created, with one level designated as the reference.\n\n```{r}\n#| label: reference-levels-table\nref_tbl <- tribble(\n  ~Attribute,                   ~`Reference level (coded 0)`,   ~`Non-reference levels (coded 1)`,\n  \"Distance to green space\",    \"15 km\",                         \"5 km; 500 m\",\n  \"Distance to shops\",          \"15 km\",                         \"5 km; 500 m\",\n  \"Distance to public transit\", \"900 m\",                         \"600 m; 300 m\",\n  \"Parking\",                    \"None\",                          \"Reserved space; Reserved garage\",\n  \"Housing cost\",               \"0% change (current cost)\",      \"−20%; +20%\"\n)\n\nflextable(ref_tbl) |>\n  bold(part = \"header\") |>\n  autofit() |>\n  theme_booktabs() |>\n  set_caption(caption = \"Reference levels for each DCE attribute\")\n```\n\nEach coefficient therefore represents the **utility change relative to the reference level**, not an absolute effect. A coefficient of 2.0 on `green5km` means \"choosing an option with green space 5 km away provides 2.0 more utility units than the same option with green space 15 km away, all else equal.\"\n\n# The non-symmetrical interval problem\n\nThis is perhaps the most fundamental challenge in comparing coefficients across levels and attributes.\n\n## Unequal physical intervals within an attribute\n\nEach dummy variable is binary (0 or 1), so on the *variable scale* all dummies look equally sized. But the physical changes they represent are not equal:\n\n```{r}\n#| label: interval-table\ninterval_tbl <- tribble(\n  ~Attribute,        ~Dummy,         ~`From (reference)`, ~`To`,    ~`Physical change`,\n  \"Green space\",     \"green5km\",     \"15 km\",             \"5 km\",   \"−10 km\",\n  \"Green space\",     \"green500m\",    \"15 km\",             \"500 m\",  \"−14.5 km\",\n  \"Shops\",           \"shops5km\",     \"15 km\",             \"5 km\",   \"−10 km\",\n  \"Shops\",           \"shops500m\",    \"15 km\",             \"500 m\",  \"−14.5 km\",\n  \"Transit\",         \"trans600\",     \"900 m\",             \"600 m\",  \"−300 m\",\n  \"Transit\",         \"trans300\",     \"900 m\",             \"300 m\",  \"−600 m\",\n  \"Parking\",         \"park_space\",   \"None\",              \"Reserved space\",   \"qualitative\",\n  \"Parking\",         \"park_garage\",  \"None\",              \"Reserved garage\",  \"qualitative\"\n)\n\nflextable(interval_tbl) |>\n  bold(part = \"header\") |>\n  merge_v(j = \"Attribute\") |>\n  valign(j = \"Attribute\", valign = \"top\") |>\n  autofit() |>\n  theme_booktabs() |>\n  set_caption(caption = \"Physical magnitude of each attribute-level dummy variable\")\n```\n\nThe ratio $\\beta_{\\text{green500m}} / \\beta_{\\text{green5km}}$ is **not** the marginal utility per kilometre of green-space proximity. It is simply the contrast between two different reference-to-level gaps — one of 14.5 km and one of 10 km. Since the DCE did not include intermediate levels (e.g. 10 km, 2 km), we cannot interpolate between them.\n\n## Incommensurable units across attributes\n\nBeyond the within-attribute problem, coefficients across attributes represent physically incomparable interventions:\n\n- $\\beta_{\\text{green5km}}$: value of reducing green-space distance by 10 km\n- $\\beta_{\\text{trans600}}$: value of reducing transit distance by 300 m\n- $\\beta_{\\text{park\\_garage}}$: value of gaining access to a reserved garage (qualitative)\n\nAll three values appear on the same utility scale, but the underlying quantities they describe — kilometres of travel, metres to a bus stop, availability of covered parking — share no common metric. Ranking attributes by coefficient magnitude does not rank them by \"how important one unit of change is\", because one unit is different for every attribute.\n\n::: {.callout-important}\n## Consequence for the reviewer's coefficient grid\n\nThe price × attribute interaction grid shows $\\beta_{pa}$ for each attribute level. These coefficients are subject to both layers of non-comparability: (1) unequal physical intervals within attributes, and (2) incommensurable units across attributes. A large $\\beta_{p, \\text{green5km}}$ relative to $\\beta_{p, \\text{trans600}}$ does not mean that price sensitivity is more strongly tied to green space than to transit — it reflects the different physical magnitudes of the underlying level differences as well.\n:::\n\n# Price coding\n\n## How price is measured\n\nThe price variable in the DCE represents a percentage change in each respondent's planned monthly housing cost. In the data:\n\n$$\n\\texttt{price\\_num} = \\frac{\\texttt{raw\\_price}}{100}, \\quad \\texttt{raw\\_price} \\in \\{-20,\\ 0,\\ +20\\}\n$$\n\nSo `price_num` ∈ {−0.2, 0, 0.2}: it is a **fraction of planned monthly cost**, not an absolute SEK amount.\n\n## Implications for coefficient interpretation\n\nA \"one-unit change\" in `price_num` would represent a 100% increase in monthly housing cost — an interval that does not appear in the data and has no practical meaning. The entire range of variation in the data is 0.4 units (from −0.2 to +0.2). The price coefficient $\\beta_p \\approx -5$ therefore means:\n\n> \"A 0.1-unit increase in `price_num` (i.e. a 10% increase in planned cost) reduces utility by approximately 0.5 units.\"\n\nThis is only interpretable once anchored to a specific planned cost level.\n\n## Individual heterogeneity in the price anchor\n\nBecause planned costs vary across respondents (median ~10,000 SEK for owners, ~9,000 SEK for renters), the price coefficient absorbs a *distribution* of individual monetary references, not a fixed SEK unit. The estimated $\\hat{\\beta}_p$ reflects an average price sensitivity across respondents with different planned costs.\n\n```{r}\n#| label: planned-cost-summary\ndf_model <- readRDS(here(\"data/formr\", \"df_model.rds\"))\nlibrary(haven)\n\ncost_summary <- df_model |>\n  mutate(\n    ägandebostad = haven::as_factor(ägandebostad),\n    Own          = if_else(ägandebostad == \"Ja\", \"Owner\", \"Renter\"),\n    planed_cost  = if_else(as.numeric(planed_cost) == 0, NA_real_, as.numeric(planed_cost))\n  ) |>\n  distinct(panelID, .keep_all = TRUE) |>\n  group_by(Own) |>\n  summarise(\n    N              = n(),\n    Median         = median(planed_cost, na.rm = TRUE),\n    Mean           = round(mean(planed_cost, na.rm = TRUE)),\n    SD             = round(sd(planed_cost, na.rm = TRUE)),\n    `10% of median (scaler)` = median(planed_cost, na.rm = TRUE) * 0.10,\n    .groups = \"drop\"\n  )\n\nflextable(cost_summary) |>\n  bold(part = \"header\") |>\n  colformat_num(j = 3:6, big.mark = \",\", digits = 0) |>\n  autofit() |>\n  theme_booktabs() |>\n  set_caption(caption = \"Planned monthly housing cost by tenure (SEK)\")\n```\n\nThe scaler used for MWTP conversion (`0.10 × median planned cost`) anchors this to a 10% change at the group median — a convention that makes MWTP values concrete but means owner and renter MWTPs are on slightly different absolute scales.\n\n# The price × attribute interaction coefficients\n\n## What they test\n\nEach interaction term takes the form:\n\n$$\n\\texttt{p\\_green5km} = \\texttt{price\\_num} \\times \\mathbb{1}[\\text{green space} = 5\\text{km}]\n$$\n\nThis variable equals `price_num` when the choice scenario includes 5 km green space, and 0 otherwise. Its coefficient $\\beta_{p,\\text{green5km}}$ therefore captures: **does the marginal disutility of a price increase change in scenarios where green space is 5 km away?**\n\n## The coefficients\n\n```{r}\n#| label: interaction-coef-table\nsig_stars <- function(p) case_when(\n  is.na(p)  ~ \"\",   p < 0.001 ~ \"***\",\n  p < 0.01  ~ \"**\", p < 0.05  ~ \"*\",\n  TRUE      ~ \"\"\n)\n\nfmt_coef <- function(est, se, p) {\n  if (is.na(est)) return(\"–\")\n  paste0(sprintf(\"%.2f\", est), sig_stars(p), \" (\", sprintf(\"%.2f\", se), \")\")\n}\n\npull_cell <- function(tdf, term_name) {\n  r <- tdf[tdf$term == term_name, ]\n  if (nrow(r) == 0) return(\"–\")\n  fmt_coef(r$estimate[1], r$std.error[1], r$p.value[1])\n}\n\ninter_map <- tribble(\n  ~label,                               ~attr_term,  ~inter_term,\n  \"Green space: 5 km (vs 15 km)\",        \"green5km\",  \"p_green5km\",\n  \"Green space: 500 m (vs 15 km)\",       \"green500m\", \"p_green500m\",\n  \"Shops: 5 km (vs 15 km)\",              \"shops5km\",  \"p_shops5km\",\n  \"Shops: 500 m (vs 15 km)\",             \"shops500m\", \"p_shops500m\",\n  \"Transit stop: 600 m (vs 900 m)\",      \"trans600\",  \"p_trans600\",\n  \"Transit stop: 300 m (vs 900 m)\",      \"trans300\",  \"p_trans300\",\n  \"Parking: reserved garage (vs none)\",  \"garage\",    \"p_garage\",\n  \"Parking: reserved space (vs none)\",   \"space\",     \"p_space\"\n)\n\nprice_section <- tibble(\n  Section   = \"Price\",\n  Attribute = \"Price\",\n  Owner     = pull_cell(tdf_own_inter,  \"price_num\"),\n  Renter    = pull_cell(tdf_rent_inter, \"price_num\")\n)\n\nattr_section <- inter_map |>\n  rowwise() |>\n  mutate(\n    Section   = \"Attribute coefficients\",\n    Attribute = label,\n    Owner     = pull_cell(tdf_own_inter,  attr_term),\n    Renter    = pull_cell(tdf_rent_inter, attr_term)\n  ) |> ungroup() |> select(Section, Attribute, Owner, Renter)\n\ninter_section <- inter_map |>\n  rowwise() |>\n  mutate(\n    Section   = \"Price \\u00d7 attribute interactions\",\n    Attribute = paste0(\"Price \\u00d7 \", label),\n    Owner     = pull_cell(tdf_own_inter,  inter_term),\n    Renter    = pull_cell(tdf_rent_inter, inter_term)\n  ) |> ungroup() |> select(Section, Attribute, Owner, Renter)\n\ngrid_df <- bind_rows(price_section, attr_section, inter_section)\nn1 <- 1; n2 <- 1 + nrow(attr_section); n3 <- n2 + nrow(inter_section)\n\nflextable(grid_df |> select(-Section)) |>\n  add_header_row(values = c(\"\", \"Owners\", \"Renters\"), colwidths = c(1, 1, 1)) |>\n  bold(part = \"header\") |>\n  align(j = 2:3, align = \"center\") |>\n  bg(i = 1,              bg = \"#e8e8e8\") |> bold(i = 1) |>\n  bg(i = seq(2, n2),     bg = \"#f7f7f7\") |>\n  bg(i = seq(n2+1, n3),  bg = \"#eef4fb\") |>\n  hline(i = n1, border = officer::fp_border(width = 1)) |>\n  hline(i = n2, border = officer::fp_border(width = 1)) |>\n  autofit() |>\n  theme_booktabs() |>\n  add_footer_lines(\"Standard errors in parentheses. * p<0.05  ** p<0.01  *** p<0.001.\\nGrey: price coefficient. Light grey: attribute main effects. Blue: price\\u00d7attribute interactions.\") |>\n  set_caption(caption = \"Coefficient grid: attribute effects and price \\u00d7 attribute interactions\")\n```\n\n## Interpreting the magnitude\n\nBecause of the issues described in Sections 3–5, the raw magnitudes of the interaction coefficients are difficult to compare. Two questions are worth asking for each term:\n\n1. **Sign:** A positive $\\beta_{pa}$ means respondents are *more* price-tolerant when that attribute level is present. A negative value means they are *more* price-sensitive. This directional reading is interpretable even when magnitudes are not.\n\n2. **Stability check:** Do the main attribute coefficients change substantially when interaction terms are added? Large shifts suggest the interaction term is absorbing part of the main effect — a sign of collinearity, not a new insight. The MWTP comparison in the next section makes this concrete.\n\n# MWTP: the recommended summary\n\nMWTP normalises the attribute effect by the price coefficient:\n\n$$\n\\text{MWTP}_a = -\\frac{\\hat{\\beta}_a}{\\hat{\\beta}_p} \\times \\underbrace{0.10 \\times \\text{median cost}}_{\\text{scaler}}\n$$\n\nThis expresses the monetary value of each attribute level in SEK/month. It resolves the price-scale problem (the fractional coding is normalised out) but does **not** resolve the non-symmetrical interval problem — the MWTP for \"green space 5 km vs 15 km\" still represents a different physical change than the MWTP for \"green space 500 m vs 15 km.\" Comparisons should always specify the counterfactual explicitly.\n\n```{r}\n#| label: mwtp-comparison\nscaler_own  <- 0.10 * 10000\nscaler_rent <- 0.10 * 9000\n\nbase_attr_map <- c(\n  \"green5km\"  = \"dist_green5km\",       \"green500m\" = \"dist_green500 meter\",\n  \"shops5km\"  = \"dist_shops5km\",       \"shops500m\" = \"dist_shops500 meter\",\n  \"trans600\"  = \"dist_trans600\",        \"trans300\"  = \"dist_trans300\",\n  \"garage\"    = \"parkingreserverad garageplats\",\n  \"space\"     = \"parkingreserverad P-plats\"\n)\n\nget_mwtp <- function(tdf_attr, tdf_price, attr_term, scaler) {\n  beta_a <- tdf_attr$estimate[tdf_attr$term == attr_term]\n  beta_p <- tdf_price$estimate[tdf_price$term == \"price_num\"]\n  if (length(beta_a) == 0 || length(beta_p) == 0) return(NA_integer_)\n  round(-(beta_a / beta_p) * scaler)\n}\n\nmwtp_tbl <- inter_map |>\n  rowwise() |>\n  mutate(\n    `Owner — baseline`    = get_mwtp(tdf_own_base,  tdf_own_base,  base_attr_map[[attr_term]], scaler_own),\n    `Owner — interaction` = get_mwtp(tdf_own_inter, tdf_own_inter, attr_term, scaler_own),\n    `Owner — diff`        = `Owner — interaction` - `Owner — baseline`,\n    `Renter — baseline`   = get_mwtp(tdf_rent_base,  tdf_rent_base,  base_attr_map[[attr_term]], scaler_rent),\n    `Renter — interaction`= get_mwtp(tdf_rent_inter, tdf_rent_inter, attr_term, scaler_rent),\n    `Renter — diff`       = `Renter — interaction` - `Renter — baseline`\n  ) |>\n  ungroup() |>\n  select(Attribute = label,\n         `Owner — baseline`, `Owner — interaction`, `Owner — diff`,\n         `Renter — baseline`, `Renter — interaction`, `Renter — diff`)\n\nflextable(mwtp_tbl) |>\n  add_header_row(\n    values    = c(\"\", \"Owners (SEK/month)\", \"Renters (SEK/month)\"),\n    colwidths = c(1, 3, 3)\n  ) |>\n  set_header_labels(\n    `Owner — baseline`     = \"Baseline\",\n    `Owner — interaction`  = \"Price\\u00d7attr model\",\n    `Owner — diff`         = \"\\u0394\",\n    `Renter — baseline`    = \"Baseline\",\n    `Renter — interaction` = \"Price\\u00d7attr model\",\n    `Renter — diff`        = \"\\u0394\"\n  ) |>\n  bold(part = \"header\") |>\n  align(j = 2:7, align = \"center\") |>\n  colformat_int(j = 2:7) |>\n  bg(j = c(4, 7), bg = \"#f0f0f0\") |>\n  color(i = ~ abs(`Owner — diff`)  > 100, j = 4, color = \"#c0392b\") |>\n  color(i = ~ abs(`Renter — diff`) > 100, j = 7, color = \"#c0392b\") |>\n  autofit() |>\n  theme_booktabs() |>\n  add_footer_lines(\"\\u0394 = (price\\u00d7attr model) \\u2212 (baseline). Values in red: |diff| > 100 SEK, suggesting the interaction term absorbs part of the main attribute effect.\") |>\n  set_caption(caption = \"MWTP comparison: baseline vs price \\u00d7 attribute interaction model (SEK/month)\")\n```\n\n# Summary and recommendation\n\nThe price × attribute coefficient grid is produced as requested. However, the coefficients should be interpreted with the following caveats in mind:\n\n1. **Reference-level dependence:** All coefficients are contrasts vs the reference level for each attribute. Changing the reference level would change all coefficients.\n\n2. **Non-symmetrical intervals:** The physical magnitude of each level difference varies within and across attributes. Raw coefficient magnitudes are not directly comparable.\n\n3. **Price scale:** `price_num` is a fraction of individual planned costs, not a fixed monetary unit. The coefficient is interpretable only after applying a scaler tied to a specific cost level.\n\n4. **Interaction term interpretation:** A significant $\\beta_{pa}$ indicates that price sensitivity shifts in the presence of attribute level $a$. Its magnitude is on a doubly-indirected scale and should not be read as a monetary quantity without the MWTP transformation.\n\n**Recommendation for the reviewer:** The MWTP table (Table 4 of the paper, reproduced above with the interaction model comparison) is the most appropriate response to the reviewer's underlying question — \"how much do respondents value each attribute?\" MWTP normalises by price sensitivity and expresses the result in a common monetary metric. The interaction model results are broadly consistent with the baseline, with MWTP estimates differing by less than 50 SEK/month for most attributes. The larger differences for green space (particularly for renters) reflect collinearity between the green-space and price terms in the renter subsample at low draw counts, and should not be treated as substantive findings.\n"},"elapsedMs":160}</script></tool-result></div>

The reviewer asked to see the price coefficient interacted with each attribute level, expressed as a grid of coefficients.\n\nThis is a legitimate specification to explore, but it raises several interpretive challenges. The baseline utility function for respondent $i$ choosing alternative $j$ in choice occasion $t$ is:\n\n$$\nU_{ijt} = \\sum_{a} \\beta_{ia} \\cdot x_{ajt} + \\beta_p \\cdot \\text{price}_{jt} + \\varepsilon_{ijt}\n$$\n\nwhere $x_{ajt}$ are dummy-coded attribute levels, $\\text{price}_{jt}$ is the price variable, and $\\beta_{ia}$ are individual-level random coefficients drawn from a multivariate normal distribution.\n\nThe **price × attribute interaction model** adds fixed interaction terms:\n\n$$\nU_{ijt} = \\sum_{a} \\beta_{ia} \\cdot x_{ajt} + \\beta_p \\cdot \\text{price}_{jt} + \\sum_{a} \\beta_{pa} \\cdot (\\text{price}_{jt} \\times x_{ajt}) + \\varepsilon_{ijt}\n$$\n\nThe additional term $\\beta_{pa}$ estimates whether the marginal disutility of price changes when a particular attribute level is present. If $\\beta_{pa} > 0$, price is *less* disutilising when that attribute level is in the scenario.\n\n# Attribute coding and reference levels\n\nAll attributes are **dummy-coded**: for each attribute with $k$ levels, $k - 1$ binary (0/1) indicator variables are created, with one level designated as the reference.\n\n```{r}\n#| label: reference-levels-table\nref_tbl <- tribble(\n  ~Attribute,                   ~`Reference level (coded 0)`,   ~`Non-reference levels (coded 1)`,\n  \"Distance to green space\",    \"15 km\",                         \"5 km; 500 m\",\n  \"Distance to shops\",          \"15 km\",                         \"5 km; 500 m\",\n  \"Distance to public transit\", \"900 m\",                         \"600 m; 300 m\",\n  \"Parking\",                    \"None\",                          \"Reserved space; Reserved garage\",\n  \"Housing cost\",               \"0% change (current cost)\",      \"−20%; +20%\"\n)\n\nflextable(ref_tbl) |>\n  bold(part = \"header\") |>\n  autofit() |>\n  theme_booktabs() |>\n  set_caption(caption = \"Reference levels for each DCE attribute\")\n```\n\nEach coefficient therefore represents the **utility change relative to the reference level**, not an absolute effect. A coefficient of 2.0 on `green5km` means \"an option with green space 5 km away is preferred by 2.0 utility units over an otherwise identical option with green space 15 km away.\"\n\n# The non-symmetrical interval problem\n\nThis is perhaps the most fundamental challenge in comparing coefficients across levels and attributes.\n\n## Unequal physical intervals within an attribute\n\nEach dummy variable is binary (0 or 1), so on the *variable scale* all dummies look equally sized. But the physical changes they represent are not equal:\n\n```{r}\n#| label: interval-table\ninterval_tbl <- tribble(\n  ~Attribute,  ~Dummy,        ~`From (reference)`, ~`To`,           ~`Physical change`,\n  \"Green space\",\"green5km\",   \"15 km\",             \"5 km\",          \"−10 km\",\n  \"Green space\",\"green500m\",  \"15 km\",             \"500 m\",         \"−14.5 km\",\n  \"Shops\",      \"shops5km\",   \"15 km\",             \"5 km\",          \"−10 km\",\n  \"Shops\",      \"shops500m\",  \"15 km\",             \"500 m\",         \"−14.5 km\",\n  \"Transit\",    \"trans600\",   \"900 m\",             \"600 m\",         \"−300 m\",\n  \"Transit\",    \"trans300\",   \"900 m\",             \"300 m\",         \"−600 m\",\n  \"Parking\",    \"park_space\", \"None\",              \"Reserved space\",\"qualitative\",\n  \"Parking\",    \"park_garage\",\"None\",              \"Reserved garage\",\"qualitative\"\n)\n\nflextable(interval_tbl) |>\n  bold(part = \"header\") |>\n  merge_v(j = \"Attribute\") |>\n  valign(j = \"Attribute\", valign = \"top\") |>\n  autofit() |>\n  theme_booktabs() |>\n  set_caption(caption = \"Physical magnitude of each attribute-level dummy variable\")\n```\n\nThe ratio $\\beta_{\\text{green500m}} / \\beta_{\\text{green5km}}$ is **not** the marginal utility per kilometre of green-space proximity. It is simply the contrast between two different reference-to-level gaps — one of 14.5 km and one of 10 km. Since the DCE did not include intermediate levels, we cannot interpolate between them.\n\n## Incommensurable units across attributes\n\nBeyond the within-attribute problem, coefficients across attributes represent physically incomparable interventions:\n\n- $\\beta_{\\text{green5km}}$: utility of reducing green-space distance by 10 km\n- $\\beta_{\\text{trans600}}$: utility of reducing transit distance by 300 m\n- $\\beta_{\\text{park\\_garage}}$: utility of gaining access to a reserved garage (qualitative)\n\nAll three values appear on the same utility scale, but the underlying quantities they describe — kilometres, metres, parking quality — share no common metric. Ranking attributes by coefficient magnitude does not rank them by \"importance\", because each coefficient reflects a physically different-sized change.\n\n::: {.callout-important}\n## Consequence for the reviewer's coefficient grid\n\nThe price × attribute interaction grid shows $\\beta_{pa}$ for each attribute level. These coefficients are subject to both layers of non-comparability: (1) unequal physical intervals within attributes, and (2) incommensurable units across attributes. A larger $\\beta_{p, \\text{green5km}}$ relative to $\\beta_{p, \\text{trans600}}$ does not mean that price sensitivity is more strongly tied to green space than to transit — it partly reflects the different physical magnitudes of the two level differences.\n:::\n\n# Price coding\n\n## How price is measured\n\nThe price variable in the DCE represents a percentage change from each respondent's planned monthly housing cost. In the model:\n\n$$\n\\texttt{price\\_num} = \\frac{\\texttt{raw\\_price}}{100}, \\quad \\texttt{raw\\_price} \\in \\{-20,\\ 0,\\ +20\\}\n$$\n\nSo `price_num` ∈ {−0.2, 0, 0.2}: it is a **fraction of planned monthly cost**, not an absolute SEK amount.\n\n## Implications for coefficient interpretation\n\nA \"one-unit change\" in `price_num` would represent a 100% cost increase — an interval that does not appear in the data. The entire observed range is 0.4 units. The price coefficient $\\beta_p \\approx -6$ means:\n\n> \"A 0.1-unit increase in `price_num` (i.e. a 10% increase in planned cost) reduces utility by approximately 0.6 units.\"\n\nThis is only interpretable once anchored to a specific planned cost level.\n\n## Individual heterogeneity in the price anchor\n\nBecause planned costs vary across respondents, the price coefficient absorbs a *distribution* of individual monetary references, not a fixed SEK unit.\n\n```{r}\n#| label: planned-cost-summary\ndf_model <- readRDS(here(\"data/formr\", \"df_model.rds\"))\n\ncost_summary <- df_model |>\n  mutate(\n    ägandebostad = haven::as_factor(ägandebostad),\n    Own          = if_else(ägandebostad == \"Ja\", \"Owner\", \"Renter\"),\n    planed_cost  = if_else(as.numeric(planed_cost) == 0, NA_real_, as.numeric(planed_cost))\n  ) |>\n  distinct(panelID, .keep_all = TRUE) |>\n  group_by(Own) |>\n  summarise(\n    N                        = n(),\n    `Median (SEK)`           = median(planed_cost, na.rm = TRUE),\n    `Mean (SEK)`             = round(mean(planed_cost, na.rm = TRUE)),\n    `SD (SEK)`               = round(sd(planed_cost, na.rm = TRUE)),\n    `10% of median (scaler)` = median(planed_cost, na.rm = TRUE) * 0.10,\n    .groups = \"drop\"\n  )\n\nflextable(cost_summary) |>\n  bold(part = \"header\") |>\n  colformat_num(j = 3:6, big.mark = \",\", digits = 0) |>\n  autofit() |>\n  theme_booktabs() |>\n  set_caption(caption = \"Planned monthly housing cost by tenure (SEK)\")\n```\n\nThe MWTP scaler (`0.10 × median planned cost`) anchors this to a 10% change at the group median — a convention that makes MWTP values concrete, but it means owner and renter MWTPs are on slightly different absolute scales.\n\n# The price × attribute interaction coefficients\n\n## What they test\n\nEach interaction term takes the form:\n\n$$\n\\texttt{p\\_green5km} = \\texttt{price\\_num} \\times \\mathbb{1}[\\text{green space} = 5\\text{km}]\n$$\n\nThis variable equals `price_num` when the scenario has 5 km green space, and 0 otherwise. Its coefficient $\\beta_{p,\\text{green5km}}$ captures: **does the marginal disutility of price change when green space is at 5 km?**\n\n## The coefficient grid\n\n```{r}\n#| label: interaction-coef-table\nsig_stars <- function(p) case_when(\n  is.na(p)   ~ \"\",\n  p < 0.001  ~ \"***\",\n  p < 0.01   ~ \"**\",\n  p < 0.05   ~ \"*\",\n  TRUE       ~ \"\"\n)\n\nfmt_coef <- function(est, se, p) {\n  if (is.na(est)) return(\"–\")\n  paste0(sprintf(\"%.2f\", est), sig_stars(p), \" (\", sprintf(\"%.2f\", se), \")\")\n}\n\npull_cell <- function(tdf, term_name) {\n  r <- tdf[tdf$term == term_name, ]\n  if (nrow(r) == 0) return(\"–\")\n  fmt_coef(r$estimate[1], r$std.error[1], r$p.value[1])\n}\n\ninter_map <- tribble(\n  ~label,                               ~attr_term,  ~inter_term,\n  \"Green space: 5 km (vs 15 km)\",        \"green5km\",  \"p_green5km\",\n  \"Green space: 500 m (vs 15 km)\",       \"green500m\", \"p_green500m\",\n  \"Shops: 5 km (vs 15 km)\",              \"shops5km\",  \"p_shops5km\",\n  \"Shops: 500 m (vs 15 km)\",             \"shops500m\", \"p_shops500m\",\n  \"Transit stop: 600 m (vs 900 m)\",      \"trans600\",  \"p_trans600\",\n  \"Transit stop: 300 m (vs 900 m)\",      \"trans300\",  \"p_trans300\",\n  \"Parking: reserved garage (vs none)\",  \"garage\",    \"p_garage\",\n  \"Parking: reserved space (vs none)\",   \"space\",     \"p_space\"\n)\n\nprice_section <- tibble(\n  Section   = \"Price\",\n  Attribute = \"Price\",\n  Owner     = pull_cell(tdf_own_inter,  \"price_num\"),\n  Renter    = pull_cell(tdf_rent_inter, \"price_num\")\n)\n\nattr_section <- inter_map |>\n  rowwise() |>\n  mutate(\n    Section   = \"Attribute coefficients\",\n    Attribute = label,\n    Owner     = pull_cell(tdf_own_inter,  attr_term),\n    Renter    = pull_cell(tdf_rent_inter, attr_term)\n  ) |> ungroup() |> select(Section, Attribute, Owner, Renter)\n\ninter_section <- inter_map |>\n  rowwise() |>\n  mutate(\n    Section   = \"Price \\u00d7 attribute interactions\",\n    Attribute = paste0(\"Price \\u00d7 \", label),\n    Owner     = pull_cell(tdf_own_inter,  inter_term),\n    Renter    = pull_cell(tdf_rent_inter, inter_term)\n  ) |> ungroup() |> select(Section, Attribute, Owner, Renter)\n\ngrid_df <- bind_rows(price_section, attr_section, inter_section)\nn1 <- 1; n2 <- 1 + nrow(attr_section); n3 <- n2 + nrow(inter_section)\n\nflextable(grid_df |> select(-Section)) |>\n  add_header_row(values = c(\"\", \"Owners\", \"Renters\"), colwidths = c(1, 1, 1)) |>\n  bold(part = \"header\") |>\n  align(j = 2:3, align = \"center\") |>\n  bg(i = 1,             bg = \"#e8e8e8\") |> bold(i = 1) |>\n  bg(i = seq(2, n2),    bg = \"#f7f7f7\") |>\n  bg(i = seq(n2+1, n3), bg = \"#eef4fb\") |>\n  hline(i = n1, border = officer::fp_border(width = 1)) |>\n  hline(i = n2, border = officer::fp_border(width = 1)) |>\n  autofit() |>\n  theme_booktabs() |>\n  add_footer_lines(paste0(\n    \"Standard errors in parentheses. * p<0.05  ** p<0.01  *** p<0.001.\\n\",\n    \"Grey: price coefficient. Light grey: attribute main effects (relative to reference level).\\n\",\n    \"Blue: price \\u00d7 attribute interaction terms (the reviewer's requested coefficients).\"\n  )) |>\n  set_caption(caption = \"Coefficient grid: attribute effects and price \\u00d7 attribute interactions\")\n```\n\n## What can and cannot be read from this grid\n\n**Sign (directional interpretation — valid):** A positive $\\beta_{pa}$ means respondents are *more* price-tolerant when that attribute level is present. A negative value means they are *more* price-sensitive in the presence of that level.\n\n**Magnitude (cross-attribute comparisons — not valid):** As discussed in Sections 3 and 4, the magnitudes are not directly comparable across attribute levels. A large $|\\beta_{pa}|$ for one attribute does not mean price sensitivity is more strongly tied to that attribute than to another with a smaller coefficient — the physical sizes of the level changes differ.\n\n# Why the interaction model does not yield MWTP in SEK\n\nIn the baseline model, MWTP is well-defined because the utility function is **linear in both the attribute and the price**:\n\n$$\n\\text{MWTP}_a = -\\frac{\\beta_a}{\\beta_p} \\times \\text{scaler}\n$$\n\nThe ratio $-\\beta_a / \\beta_p$ is a constant — it does not depend on the values of other variables in the choice scenario.\n\nIn the price × attribute interaction model, however, the picture changes. The partial derivative of utility with respect to the attribute is:\n\n$$\n\\frac{\\partial U}{\\partial x_a} = \\beta_a + \\beta_{pa} \\cdot \\text{price\\_num}\n$$\n\nThe marginal utility of the attribute now **depends on the price level in the scenario**. Similarly, the effective price coefficient when attribute $a$ is present is $\\beta_p + \\beta_{pa}$. The MWTP therefore varies depending on which price scenario ($-0.2$, $0$, or $+0.2$) accompanies the attribute level — it is no longer a single number.\n\n::: {.callout-warning}\n## MWTP cannot be read from the interaction model\n\nAny attempt to compute a single MWTP from the price × attribute model requires choosing a specific price level at which to evaluate the derivative — an arbitrary decision that would drive the result. The values are not interpretable in SEK without this assumption.\n\nThis is a further reason why the baseline model (which produces clean, scenario-independent MWTP estimates) is the preferred specification for the paper's main results.\n:::\n\n# MWTP from the baseline model\n\nSince the interaction model does not produce clean MWTP values, the table below shows the baseline MWTP (from Table 4 of the paper) — the recommended summary of attribute valuation.\n\n```{r}\n#| label: baseline-mwtp-table\nscaler_own  <- 0.10 * 10000\nscaler_rent <- 0.10 * 9000\n\nbase_attr_map <- c(\n  \"green5km\"  = \"dist_green5km\",\n  \"green500m\" = \"dist_green500 meter\",\n  \"shops5km\"  = \"dist_shops5km\",\n  \"shops500m\" = \"dist_shops500 meter\",\n  \"trans600\"  = \"dist_trans600\",\n  \"trans300\"  = \"dist_trans300\",\n  \"garage\"    = \"parkingreserverad garageplats\",\n  \"space\"     = \"parkingreserverad P-plats\"\n)\n\nget_mwtp <- function(tdf, attr_term, scaler) {\n  beta_a <- tdf$estimate[tdf$term == attr_term]\n  beta_p <- tdf$estimate[tdf$term == \"price_num\"]\n  if (length(beta_a) == 0 || length(beta_p) == 0) return(NA_integer_)\n  round(-(beta_a / beta_p) * scaler)\n}\n\nmwtp_tbl <- inter_map |>\n  rowwise() |>\n  mutate(\n    `Owner MWTP`  = get_mwtp(tdf_own_base,  base_attr_map[[attr_term]], scaler_own),\n    `Renter MWTP` = get_mwtp(tdf_rent_base, base_attr_map[[attr_term]], scaler_rent)\n  ) |>\n  ungroup() |>\n  select(Attribute = label, `Owner MWTP`, `Renter MWTP`)\n\nflextable(mwtp_tbl) |>\n  add_header_row(\n    values    = c(\"\", \"Baseline model (SEK/month)\"),\n    colwidths = c(1, 2)\n  ) |>\n  bold(part = \"header\") |>\n  align(j = 2:3, align = \"center\") |>\n  colformat_int(j = 2:3) |>\n  autofit() |>\n  theme_booktabs() |>\n  add_footer_lines(paste0(\n    \"MWTP = \\u2212(\\u03b2_attribute / \\u03b2_price) \\u00d7 scaler.\\n\",\n    \"Scaler: 10% of median monthly planned housing cost (owners: 10,000 SEK; renters: 9,000 SEK).\\n\",\n    \"Interpretation: estimated SEK/month a respondent would accept as a cost increase\\n\",\n    \"in exchange for the stated improvement in each attribute, relative to its reference level.\"\n  )) |>\n  set_caption(caption = \"MWTP estimates from the baseline mixed logit model (Table 4 of the paper)\")\n```\n\nThese values answer the reviewer's underlying question — \"how much do respondents value each attribute?\" — in a monetarily interpretable way. The price × attribute coefficient grid (Section 5) provides additional information about whether price sensitivity varies with attribute levels, but it operates on the utility scale rather than a monetary scale and should be treated as supplementary.\n\n# Summary and recommendation\n\nThe price × attribute coefficient grid is produced as requested. The key interpretive points are:\n\n1. **Reference-level dependence:** All coefficients are contrasts vs the reference level. Changing the reference level changes all coefficients.\n\n2. **Non-symmetrical intervals:** Each dummy represents a different-sized physical change. Coefficient magnitudes are not directly comparable across levels or attributes.\n\n3. **Price scale:** `price_num` is a fraction of individual planned costs, not a fixed monetary unit. Raw price coefficients are only interpretable after applying a scaler.\n\n4. **No clean MWTP from the interaction model:** Because the marginal utility of an attribute depends on the price level in the interaction model ($\\partial U / \\partial x_a = \\beta_a + \\beta_{pa} \\cdot \\text{price}$), MWTP is not a scenario-independent quantity. The formula $-\\beta_a / \\beta_p$ does not apply.\n\n**Recommendation:** The MWTP table from the baseline model (reproduced in Section 7) directly answers the reviewer's question and should be the primary response. The price × attribute coefficient grid can accompany it as a supplementary specification check, with the caveats above noted clearly.\n"}}</script></tool-call></div>

<div><thinking id="thinking-1774873878561-7fpat">
The user is asking a question about the coefficient grid — specifically noting that no interaction terms appear to be significant. This is likely because the models were estimated with only 20 draws, which gives very imprecise estimates with large standard errors. With 20 draws, the estimates are noisy and significance tests won't be reliable.

This is a key point to make. The user is right to notice this. The lack of significant interaction terms is almost certainly an artifact of:

1. **Very few draws (20)**: The models were estimated with `numDraws = 20` specifically to make them run fast. This produces highly imprecise estimates. 

The baseline models used 1000 draws for owners and 100 for renters, so dropping to 20 inflates standard errors dramatically. Beyond the estimation precision issue, there's also the underlying economics — with an orthogonal design, price and attributes aren't correlated by construction, so interaction terms may genuinely be weak. Plus the renter sample is only 167 observations, which limits power for detecting interactions.

The main takeaway is that re-estimating with more draws is essential before concluding anything about these interaction effects.
</thinking></div>

Almost certainly yes — and the reason is the 20-draw estimation. Here's the full picture:

**Primary cause — 20 draws is far too few for reliable inference.** The models were estimated quickly with `numDraws = 20` specifically to avoid waiting. With so few simulation draws, the likelihood approximation is very noisy, which inflates standard errors substantially. The result is wide confidence intervals on every coefficient, and nothing clears a significance threshold. The baseline models used 1000 draws (owners) and 100 draws (renters) — far more appropriate for inference. At 20 draws you can trust the sign and rough magnitude of the estimates, but not the standard errors.

**Secondary cause — orthogonal design.** In a well-designed DCE, price and attributes are orthogonal by construction — they are assigned independently across choice occasions. This means there is no built-in variation in price *conditional on* an attribute level, which makes the interactions harder to detect. Power for these terms will naturally be lower than for main effects.

**Third — they may genuinely not be significant.** Even with proper estimation, it's entirely plausible that price sensitivity does not vary systematically with attribute levels. If people process price as a separate dimension from location/parking attributes (which is economically reasonable), the interactions would be near zero.

The plan to address this properly:

This produces inflated standard errors and renders\nall interaction coefficients non-significant — an artifact of the estimation, not necessarily the data.\n\n---\n\n## Three reasons for the lack of significance (in likely order of importance)\n\n1. **20 draws → noisy likelihood approximation → inflated SEs.** The baseline models used 1000 (owners)\n   and 100 (renters) draws. At 20 draws, standard errors are unreliable and significance tests are\n   essentially meaningless.\n\n2. **Orthogonal design.** Price and attributes are assigned independently across choice occasions by\n   construction. There is no built-in correlation between price levels and attribute levels, so detecting\n   price × attribute interactions requires genuine within-respondent variation in price sensitivity.\n   Statistical power for these terms is naturally lower than for main effects.\n\n3. **True null.** Even with proper estimation, respondents may process price as a separate dimension from\n   location/parking attributes — in which case the interactions are genuinely near zero.\n\n---\n\n## What to do\n\n### Step 1 — Re-estimate with adequate draws\nRe-estimate the two interaction models with `numDraws = 500` (same as the planned value before it was\nreduced). <div><tool-call id="toolu_018Hgk41eNq4jszb42T2wQgk"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"name":"write","input":{"file_path":"C:/Users/ni3054ch/.positai/plans/2026-03-30-1055-plan.md","content":"# Plan: Heatmap coefficient grid + comparability text in Quarto doc\n**Date:** 2026-03-30\n\n...[truncated, total 3737 chars]","overwrite":true},"caption":"C:/Users/ni3054ch/.positai/plans/2026-03-30-1055-plan.md","inputPreview":{"type":"code","value":"# Plan: Heatmap coefficient grid + comparability text in Quarto doc\n**Date:** 2026-03-30\n\n---\n\n## What to add\n\nA new subsection inside Section 5 (\"The price × attribute interaction coefficients\") of\n`docs/reviewer_note_price_interactions.qmd`, after the existing coefficient grid table.\n\n### New subsection: \"Visual representation — coefficient heatmap\"\n\n#### The heatmap\n\nBuilt with `ggplot2::geom_tile()`. Two separate panels stacked vertically:\n\n**Panel A — Attribute main effects**\n- Rows: 8 attribute levels (green5km, green500m, shops5km, shops500m, trans600, trans300,\n  park_garage, park_space), grouped visually by parent attribute\n- Columns: Owners | Renters\n- Fill colour: coefficient value on a diverging scale (blue → white → red),\n  centred at zero\n- Text overlay on each tile: coefficient to 2 dp + significance stars\n  (or \"n.s.\" if p ≥ 0.05)\n\n**Panel B — Price × attribute interactions**\n- Same row/column structure as Panel A\n- Same colour scale (so magnitude is visually comparable within each panel)\n- Same text overlay format\n\nThe two panels share the same colour scale and are stacked with a clear label dividing them, \nso the reader can scan across both.\n\n#### The \"why these cannot be compared\" callout\n\nImmediately after the heatmap, a `{.callout-warning}` block with the heading\n**\"Why the colours cannot be directly compared\"**, covering:\n\n1. **Different physical magnitudes per tile:** Each row represents a different-sized real-world\n   change. A deep red for `green5km` (10 km improvement) and a deep red for `trans300`\n   (600 m improvement) look identical on the heatmap but represent interventions that differ\n   by a factor of ~17 in physical distance — and are in different units entirely.\n\n2. **Qualitative vs quantitative levels:** The parking rows represent a qualitative step\n   (none → reserved space → reserved garage) with no natural metric. Colour intensity has\n   no physical interpretation there.\n\n3. **Price not on an absolute scale:** The price coefficient — and therefore the price ×\n   attribute interaction coefficients — is anchored to individual planned costs, not a fixed\n   SEK amount. Comparing the magnitude of `p_green5km` to `p_trans600` on the colour scale\n   is similarly uninformative.\n\n4. **What the heatmap IS useful for:** Within a single cell, the sign and rough significance\n   tell you the direction of the effect. Comparing the same attribute across Owners vs Renters\n   (same row, two columns) is meaningful — same physical change, different groups.\n\n---\n\n## Implementation notes\n\n- Add a new code cell labelled `coef-heatmap` in the Quarto doc after the `interaction-coef-table`\n  cell\n- Data for the heatmap is derived from `tdf_own_inter` and `tdf_rent_inter` (already loaded)\n- Use `ggplot2` (already in the `pacman` load list — add if not present)\n- Significance stars derived from p-values using the same `sig_stars()` helper already defined\n- Colour scale: `scale_fill_gradient2(low = \"#2166ac\", mid = \"white\", high = \"#d6604d\", midpoint = 0)`\n- `geom_text()` overlay with coefficient + stars\n- `facet_wrap(~ panel, ncol = 1, scales = \"free_y\")` to stack the two panels\n\n---\n\n## Draw-count caveat\n\nAlso add a short `{.callout-note}` at the top of Section 5 (before the table) noting that:\n- Models were estimated with 20 simulation draws for speed\n- Standard errors and significance stars should be treated as approximate\n- Re-estimation with ≥ 500 draws is recommended before drawing inferential conclusions\n\n---\n\n## Files to modify\n\n| File | Change |\n|---|---|\n| `docs/reviewer_note_price_interactions.qmd` | Add `coef-heatmap` code cell + callout warning after the grid table; add draw-count caveat callout before the table |\n\nNo other files need to change.\n"}}</script></tool-call></div>

<div><tool-result call-id="toolu_01WPoPY5owSrGuUa1xkwvadG"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"status":"success","result":{"type":"text","value":"[File: 18.5KB, 393 lines, showing lines 1-393]\n     1→---\n     2→title: \"Interpreting pric...[truncated, total 21639 chars]"},"resultPreview":{"type":"code","value":"[File: 18.5KB, 393 lines, showing lines 1-393]\n---\ntitle: \"Interpreting price × attribute interaction coefficients in a discrete choice experiment\"\nsubtitle: \"A methodological note for reviewer response\"\ndate: today\nformat:\n  html:\n    self-contained: true\n    toc: true\n    toc-depth: 3\n    theme: cosmo\nexecute:\n  echo: false\n  warning: false\n  message: false\n---\n\n::: {.callout-note}\nThis report was generated using AI under general human direction. At the time of generation, the contents have not been comprehensively reviewed by a human analyst.\n\n<\!--\nTo indicate human review: Delete the line above about contents not being reviewed, and replace this comment with:\nThe contents have been reviewed and validated by [Your Name], [Your Role] on [Date].\n-->\n:::\n\n# Overview\n\nThis note accompanies the price × attribute interaction analysis produced in response to a reviewer request. The reviewer asked to see the price coefficient interacted with each attribute level, expressed as a grid of coefficients.\n\nThis is a legitimate specification to explore, but it raises several interpretive challenges. Most importantly, the price × attribute interaction model **does not produce MWTP estimates in SEK** — the interaction terms break the standard MWTP formula. This note works through each challenge in turn, and concludes that the MWTP estimates from the baseline model (Tables 3–4 of the paper) remain the most appropriate summary of how respondents value each attribute.\n\n```{r}\n#| label: load-packages\nlibrary(pacman)\np_load(here, broom, logitr, dplyr, tidyr, stringr, flextable, tibble, knitr, haven)\n```\n\n```{r}\n#| label: load-data\nmxl_own_base   <- readRDS(here(\"output/models\", \"mxl_owner_base.rds\"))\nmxl_rent_base  <- readRDS(here(\"output/models\", \"mxl_renter_base.rds\"))\nmxl_own_inter  <- readRDS(here(\"output/models\", \"mxl_price_attr_own.rds\"))\nmxl_rent_inter <- readRDS(here(\"output/models\", \"mxl_price_attr_rent.rds\"))\n\ntdf_own_base   <- broom::tidy(mxl_own_base)   |> filter(!str_starts(term, \"sd_\"))\ntdf_rent_base  <- broom::tidy(mxl_rent_base)  |> filter(!str_starts(term, \"sd_\"))\ntdf_own_inter  <- broom::tidy(mxl_own_inter)  |> filter(!str_starts(term, \"sd_\"))\ntdf_rent_inter <- broom::tidy(mxl_rent_inter) |> filter(!str_starts(term, \"sd_\"))\n```\n\n# Model specification\n\nThe paper uses a mixed logit (MXL) model with correlated random parameters. The baseline utility function for respondent $i$ choosing alternative $j$ in choice occasion $t$ is:\n\n$$\nU_{ijt} = \\sum_{a} \\beta_{ia} \\cdot x_{ajt} + \\beta_p \\cdot \\text{price}_{jt} + \\varepsilon_{ijt}\n$$\n\nwhere $x_{ajt}$ are dummy-coded attribute levels, $\\text{price}_{jt}$ is the price variable, and $\\beta_{ia}$ are individual-level random coefficients drawn from a multivariate normal distribution.\n\nThe **price × attribute interaction model** adds fixed interaction terms:\n\n$$\nU_{ijt} = \\sum_{a} \\beta_{ia} \\cdot x_{ajt} + \\beta_p \\cdot \\text{price}_{jt} + \\sum_{a} \\beta_{pa} \\cdot (\\text{price}_{jt} \\times x_{ajt}) + \\varepsilon_{ijt}\n$$\n\nThe additional term $\\beta_{pa}$ estimates whether the marginal disutility of price changes when a particular attribute level is present. If $\\beta_{pa} > 0$, price is *less* disutilising when that attribute level is in the scenario.\n\n# Attribute coding and reference levels\n\nAll attributes are **dummy-coded**: for each attribute with $k$ levels, $k - 1$ binary (0/1) indicator variables are created, with one level designated as the reference.\n\n```{r}\n#| label: reference-levels-table\nref_tbl <- tribble(\n  ~Attribute,                   ~`Reference level (coded 0)`,   ~`Non-reference levels (coded 1)`,\n  \"Distance to green space\",    \"15 km\",                         \"5 km; 500 m\",\n  \"Distance to shops\",          \"15 km\",                         \"5 km; 500 m\",\n  \"Distance to public transit\", \"900 m\",                         \"600 m; 300 m\",\n  \"Parking\",                    \"None\",                          \"Reserved space; Reserved garage\",\n  \"Housing cost\",               \"0% change (current cost)\",      \"−20%; +20%\"\n)\n\nflextable(ref_tbl) |>\n  bold(part = \"header\") |>\n  autofit() |>\n  theme_booktabs() |>\n  set_caption(caption = \"Reference levels for each DCE attribute\")\n```\n\nEach coefficient therefore represents the **utility change relative to the reference level**, not an absolute effect. A coefficient of 2.0 on `green5km` means \"an option with green space 5 km away is preferred by 2.0 utility units over an otherwise identical option with green space 15 km away.\"\n\n# The non-symmetrical interval problem\n\nThis is perhaps the most fundamental challenge in comparing coefficients across levels and attributes.\n\n## Unequal physical intervals within an attribute\n\nEach dummy variable is binary (0 or 1), so on the *variable scale* all dummies look equally sized. But the physical changes they represent are not equal:\n\n```{r}\n#| label: interval-table\ninterval_tbl <- tribble(\n  ~Attribute,  ~Dummy,        ~`From (reference)`, ~`To`,           ~`Physical change`,\n  \"Green space\",\"green5km\",   \"15 km\",             \"5 km\",          \"−10 km\",\n  \"Green space\",\"green500m\",  \"15 km\",             \"500 m\",         \"−14.5 km\",\n  \"Shops\",      \"shops5km\",   \"15 km\",             \"5 km\",          \"−10 km\",\n  \"Shops\",      \"shops500m\",  \"15 km\",             \"500 m\",         \"−14.5 km\",\n  \"Transit\",    \"trans600\",   \"900 m\",             \"600 m\",         \"−300 m\",\n  \"Transit\",    \"trans300\",   \"900 m\",             \"300 m\",         \"−600 m\",\n  \"Parking\",    \"park_space\", \"None\",              \"Reserved space\",\"qualitative\",\n  \"Parking\",    \"park_garage\",\"None\",              \"Reserved garage\",\"qualitative\"\n)\n\nflextable(interval_tbl) |>\n  bold(part = \"header\") |>\n  merge_v(j = \"Attribute\") |>\n  valign(j = \"Attribute\", valign = \"top\") |>\n  autofit() |>\n  theme_booktabs() |>\n  set_caption(caption = \"Physical magnitude of each attribute-level dummy variable\")\n```\n\nThe ratio $\\beta_{\\text{green500m}} / \\beta_{\\text{green5km}}$ is **not** the marginal utility per kilometre of green-space proximity. It is simply the contrast between two different reference-to-level gaps — one of 14.5 km and one of 10 km. Since the DCE did not include intermediate levels, we cannot interpolate between them.\n\n## Incommensurable units across attributes\n\nBeyond the within-attribute problem, coefficients across attributes represent physically incomparable interventions:\n\n- $\\beta_{\\text{green5km}}$: utility of reducing green-space distance by 10 km\n- $\\beta_{\\text{trans600}}$: utility of reducing transit distance by 300 m\n- $\\beta_{\\text{park\\_garage}}$: utility of gaining access to a reserved garage (qualitative)\n\nAll three values appear on the same utility scale, but the underlying quantities they describe — kilometres, metres, parking quality — share no common metric. Ranking attributes by coefficient magnitude does not rank them by \"importance\", because each coefficient reflects a physically different-sized change.\n\n::: {.callout-important}\n## Consequence for the reviewer's coefficient grid\n\nThe price × attribute interaction grid shows $\\beta_{pa}$ for each attribute level. These coefficients are subject to both layers of non-comparability: (1) unequal physical intervals within attributes, and (2) incommensurable units across attributes. A larger $\\beta_{p, \\text{green5km}}$ relative to $\\beta_{p, \\text{trans600}}$ does not mean that price sensitivity is more strongly tied to green space than to transit — it partly reflects the different physical magnitudes of the two level differences.\n:::\n\n# Price coding\n\n## How price is measured\n\nThe price variable in the DCE represents a percentage change from each respondent's planned monthly housing cost. In the model:\n\n$$\n\\texttt{price\\_num} = \\frac{\\texttt{raw\\_price}}{100}, \\quad \\texttt{raw\\_price} \\in \\{-20,\\ 0,\\ +20\\}\n$$\n\nSo `price_num` ∈ {−0.2, 0, 0.2}: it is a **fraction of planned monthly cost**, not an absolute SEK amount.\n\n## Implications for coefficient interpretation\n\nA \"one-unit change\" in `price_num` would represent a 100% cost increase — an interval that does not appear in the data. The entire observed range is 0.4 units. The price coefficient $\\beta_p \\approx -6$ means:\n\n> \"A 0.1-unit increase in `price_num` (i.e. a 10% increase in planned cost) reduces utility by approximately 0.6 units.\"\n\nThis is only interpretable once anchored to a specific planned cost level.\n\n## Individual heterogeneity in the price anchor\n\nBecause planned costs vary across respondents, the price coefficient absorbs a *distribution* of individual monetary references, not a fixed SEK unit.\n\n```{r}\n#| label: planned-cost-summary\ndf_model <- readRDS(here(\"data/formr\", \"df_model.rds\"))\n\ncost_summary <- df_model |>\n  mutate(\n    ägandebostad = haven::as_factor(ägandebostad),\n    Own          = if_else(ägandebostad == \"Ja\", \"Owner\", \"Renter\"),\n    planed_cost  = if_else(as.numeric(planed_cost) == 0, NA_real_, as.numeric(planed_cost))\n  ) |>\n  distinct(panelID, .keep_all = TRUE) |>\n  group_by(Own) |>\n  summarise(\n    N                        = n(),\n    `Median (SEK)`           = median(planed_cost, na.rm = TRUE),\n    `Mean (SEK)`             = round(mean(planed_cost, na.rm = TRUE)),\n    `SD (SEK)`               = round(sd(planed_cost, na.rm = TRUE)),\n    `10% of median (scaler)` = median(planed_cost, na.rm = TRUE) * 0.10,\n    .groups = \"drop\"\n  )\n\nflextable(cost_summary) |>\n  bold(part = \"header\") |>\n  colformat_num(j = 3:6, big.mark = \",\", digits = 0) |>\n  autofit() |>\n  theme_booktabs() |>\n  set_caption(caption = \"Planned monthly housing cost by tenure (SEK)\")\n```\n\nThe MWTP scaler (`0.10 × median planned cost`) anchors this to a 10% change at the group median — a convention that makes MWTP values concrete, but it means owner and renter MWTPs are on slightly different absolute scales.\n\n# The price × attribute interaction coefficients\n\n## What they test\n\nEach interaction term takes the form:\n\n$$\n\\texttt{p\\_green5km} = \\texttt{price\\_num} \\times \\mathbb{1}[\\text{green space} = 5\\text{km}]\n$$\n\nThis variable equals `price_num` when the scenario has 5 km green space, and 0 otherwise. Its coefficient $\\beta_{p,\\text{green5km}}$ captures: **does the marginal disutility of price change when green space is at 5 km?**\n\n## The coefficient grid\n\n```{r}\n#| label: interaction-coef-table\nsig_stars <- function(p) case_when(\n  is.na(p)   ~ \"\",\n  p < 0.001  ~ \"***\",\n  p < 0.01   ~ \"**\",\n  p < 0.05   ~ \"*\",\n  TRUE       ~ \"\"\n)\n\nfmt_coef <- function(est, se, p) {\n  if (is.na(est)) return(\"–\")\n  paste0(sprintf(\"%.2f\", est), sig_stars(p), \" (\", sprintf(\"%.2f\", se), \")\")\n}\n\npull_cell <- function(tdf, term_name) {\n  r <- tdf[tdf$term == term_name, ]\n  if (nrow(r) == 0) return(\"–\")\n  fmt_coef(r$estimate[1], r$std.error[1], r$p.value[1])\n}\n\ninter_map <- tribble(\n  ~label,                               ~attr_term,  ~inter_term,\n  \"Green space: 5 km (vs 15 km)\",        \"green5km\",  \"p_green5km\",\n  \"Green space: 500 m (vs 15 km)\",       \"green500m\", \"p_green500m\",\n  \"Shops: 5 km (vs 15 km)\",              \"shops5km\",  \"p_shops5km\",\n  \"Shops: 500 m (vs 15 km)\",             \"shops500m\", \"p_shops500m\",\n  \"Transit stop: 600 m (vs 900 m)\",      \"trans600\",  \"p_trans600\",\n  \"Transit stop: 300 m (vs 900 m)\",      \"trans300\",  \"p_trans300\",\n  \"Parking: reserved garage (vs none)\",  \"garage\",    \"p_garage\",\n  \"Parking: reserved space (vs none)\",   \"space\",     \"p_space\"\n)\n\nprice_section <- tibble(\n  Section   = \"Price\",\n  Attribute = \"Price\",\n  Owner     = pull_cell(tdf_own_inter,  \"price_num\"),\n  Renter    = pull_cell(tdf_rent_inter, \"price_num\")\n)\n\nattr_section <- inter_map |>\n  rowwise() |>\n  mutate(\n    Section   = \"Attribute coefficients\",\n    Attribute = label,\n    Owner     = pull_cell(tdf_own_inter,  attr_term),\n    Renter    = pull_cell(tdf_rent_inter, attr_term)\n  ) |> ungroup() |> select(Section, Attribute, Owner, Renter)\n\ninter_section <- inter_map |>\n  rowwise() |>\n  mutate(\n    Section   = \"Price \\u00d7 attribute interactions\",\n    Attribute = paste0(\"Price \\u00d7 \", label),\n    Owner     = pull_cell(tdf_own_inter,  inter_term),\n    Renter    = pull_cell(tdf_rent_inter, inter_term)\n  ) |> ungroup() |> select(Section, Attribute, Owner, Renter)\n\ngrid_df <- bind_rows(price_section, attr_section, inter_section)\nn1 <- 1; n2 <- 1 + nrow(attr_section); n3 <- n2 + nrow(inter_section)\n\nflextable(grid_df |> select(-Section)) |>\n  add_header_row(values = c(\"\", \"Owners\", \"Renters\"), colwidths = c(1, 1, 1)) |>\n  bold(part = \"header\") |>\n  align(j = 2:3, align = \"center\") |>\n  bg(i = 1,             bg = \"#e8e8e8\") |> bold(i = 1) |>\n  bg(i = seq(2, n2),    bg = \"#f7f7f7\") |>\n  bg(i = seq(n2+1, n3), bg = \"#eef4fb\") |>\n  hline(i = n1, border = officer::fp_border(width = 1)) |>\n  hline(i = n2, border = officer::fp_border(width = 1)) |>\n  autofit() |>\n  theme_booktabs() |>\n  add_footer_lines(paste0(\n    \"Standard errors in parentheses. * p<0.05  ** p<0.01  *** p<0.001.\\n\",\n    \"Grey: price coefficient. Light grey: attribute main effects (relative to reference level).\\n\",\n    \"Blue: price \\u00d7 attribute interaction terms (the reviewer's requested coefficients).\"\n  )) |>\n  set_caption(caption = \"Coefficient grid: attribute effects and price \\u00d7 attribute interactions\")\n```\n\n## What can and cannot be read from this grid\n\n**Sign (directional interpretation — valid):** A positive $\\beta_{pa}$ means respondents are *more* price-tolerant when that attribute level is present. A negative value means they are *more* price-sensitive in the presence of that level.\n\n**Magnitude (cross-attribute comparisons — not valid):** As discussed in Sections 3 and 4, the magnitudes are not directly comparable across attribute levels. A large $|\\beta_{pa}|$ for one attribute does not mean price sensitivity is more strongly tied to that attribute than to another with a smaller coefficient — the physical sizes of the level changes differ.\n\n# Why the interaction model does not yield MWTP in SEK\n\nIn the baseline model, MWTP is well-defined because the utility function is **linear in both the attribute and the price**:\n\n$$\n\\text{MWTP}_a = -\\frac{\\beta_a}{\\beta_p} \\times \\text{scaler}\n$$\n\nThe ratio $-\\beta_a / \\beta_p$ is a constant — it does not depend on the values of other variables in the choice scenario.\n\nIn the price × attribute interaction model, however, the picture changes. The partial derivative of utility with respect to the attribute is:\n\n$$\n\\frac{\\partial U}{\\partial x_a} = \\beta_a + \\beta_{pa} \\cdot \\text{price\\_num}\n$$\n\nThe marginal utility of the attribute now **depends on the price level in the scenario**. Similarly, the effective price coefficient when attribute $a$ is present is $\\beta_p + \\beta_{pa}$. The MWTP therefore varies depending on which price scenario ($-0.2$, $0$, or $+0.2$) accompanies the attribute level — it is no longer a single number.\n\n::: {.callout-warning}\n## MWTP cannot be read from the interaction model\n\nAny attempt to compute a single MWTP from the price × attribute model requires choosing a specific price level at which to evaluate the derivative — an arbitrary decision that would drive the result. The values are not interpretable in SEK without this assumption.\n\nThis is a further reason why the baseline model (which produces clean, scenario-independent MWTP estimates) is the preferred specification for the paper's main results.\n:::\n\n# MWTP from the baseline model\n\nSince the interaction model does not produce clean MWTP values, the table below shows the baseline MWTP (from Table 4 of the paper) — the recommended summary of attribute valuation.\n\n```{r}\n#| label: baseline-mwtp-table\nscaler_own  <- 0.10 * 10000\nscaler_rent <- 0.10 * 9000\n\nbase_attr_map <- c(\n  \"green5km\"  = \"dist_green5km\",\n  \"green500m\" = \"dist_green500 meter\",\n  \"shops5km\"  = \"dist_shops5km\",\n  \"shops500m\" = \"dist_shops500 meter\",\n  \"trans600\"  = \"dist_trans600\",\n  \"trans300\"  = \"dist_trans300\",\n  \"garage\"    = \"parkingreserverad garageplats\",\n  \"space\"     = \"parkingreserverad P-plats\"\n)\n\nget_mwtp <- function(tdf, attr_term, scaler) {\n  beta_a <- tdf$estimate[tdf$term == attr_term]\n  beta_p <- tdf$estimate[tdf$term == \"price_num\"]\n  if (length(beta_a) == 0 || length(beta_p) == 0) return(NA_integer_)\n  round(-(beta_a / beta_p) * scaler)\n}\n\nmwtp_tbl <- inter_map |>\n  rowwise() |>\n  mutate(\n    `Owner MWTP`  = get_mwtp(tdf_own_base,  base_attr_map[[attr_term]], scaler_own),\n    `Renter MWTP` = get_mwtp(tdf_rent_base, base_attr_map[[attr_term]], scaler_rent)\n  ) |>\n  ungroup() |>\n  select(Attribute = label, `Owner MWTP`, `Renter MWTP`)\n\nflextable(mwtp_tbl) |>\n  add_header_row(\n    values    = c(\"\", \"Baseline model (SEK/month)\"),\n    colwidths = c(1, 2)\n  ) |>\n  bold(part = \"header\") |>\n  align(j = 2:3, align = \"center\") |>\n  colformat_int(j = 2:3) |>\n  autofit() |>\n  theme_booktabs() |>\n  add_footer_lines(paste0(\n    \"MWTP = \\u2212(\\u03b2_attribute / \\u03b2_price) \\u00d7 scaler.\\n\",\n    \"Scaler: 10% of median monthly planned housing cost (owners: 10,000 SEK; renters: 9,000 SEK).\\n\",\n    \"Interpretation: estimated SEK/month a respondent would accept as a cost increase\\n\",\n    \"in exchange for the stated improvement in each attribute, relative to its reference level.\"\n  )) |>\n  set_caption(caption = \"MWTP estimates from the baseline mixed logit model (Table 4 of the paper)\")\n```\n\nThese values answer the reviewer's underlying question — \"how much do respondents value each attribute?\" — in a monetarily interpretable way. The price × attribute coefficient grid (Section 5) provides additional information about whether price sensitivity varies with attribute levels, but it operates on the utility scale rather than a monetary scale and should be treated as supplementary.\n\n# Summary and recommendation\n\nThe price × attribute coefficient grid is produced as requested. The key interpretive points are:\n\n1. **Reference-level dependence:** All coefficients are contrasts vs the reference level. Changing the reference level changes all coefficients.\n\n2. **Non-symmetrical intervals:** Each dummy represents a different-sized physical change. Coefficient magnitudes are not directly comparable across levels or attributes.\n\n3. **Price scale:** `price_num` is a fraction of individual planned costs, not a fixed monetary unit. Raw price coefficients are only interpretable after applying a scaler.\n\n4. **No clean MWTP from the interaction model:** Because the marginal utility of an attribute depends on the price level in the interaction model ($\\partial U / \\partial x_a = \\beta_a + \\beta_{pa} \\cdot \\text{price}$), MWTP is not a scenario-independent quantity. The formula $-\\beta_a / \\beta_p$ does not apply.\n\n**Recommendation:** The MWTP table from the baseline model (reproduced in Section 7) directly answers the reviewer's question and should be the primary response. The price × attribute coefficient grid can accompany it as a supplementary specification check, with the caveats above noted clearly.\n"},"elapsedMs":70}</script></tool-result></div>

Significance stars: * p<0.05  ** p<0.01  *** p<0.001.\"\n+#| fig-height: 10\n+#| fig-width: 6\n+\n+make_heat_rows <- function(tdf, group_label, panel_label, term_vec) {\n+  tibble(level = select(level, group, panel, estimate, txt)\n+}\n+\n+panel_a <- \"Panel A \\u2014 Attribute main effects\"\n+panel_b <- \"Panel B \\u2014 Price \\u00d7 attribute interactions\"\n+\n+heat_df <- bind_rows(\n+  make_heat_rows(tdf_own_inter,  \"Owners\",  panel_a, inter_map$attr_term),\n+  make_heat_rows(tdf_rent_inter, \"Renters\", panel_a, inter_map$attr_term),\n+  make_heat_rows(tdf_own_inter,  \"Owners\",  panel_b, inter_map$inter_term),\n+  make_heat_rows(tdf_rent_inter, \"Renters\", panel_b, inter_map$inter_term)\n+) |>\n+  mutate(\n+    level = factor(level, levels = rev(inter_map$label)),\n+    group = factor(group, levels = c(\"Owners\", \"Renters\")),\n+    panel = factor(panel, levels = c(panel_a, panel_b))\n+  )\n+\n+ggplot(heat_df, aes(x = group, y = level, fill = estimate)) +\n+  geom_tile(colour = \"white\", linewidth = 0.5) +\n+  geom_text(aes(label = txt), size = 3) +\n+  facet_wrap(~ panel, ncol = 1, scales = \"free_y\") +\n+  scale_fill_gradient2(\n+    low      = \"#2166ac\",\n+    mid      = \"white\",\n+    high     = \"#d6604d\",\n+    midpoint = 0,\n+    name     = \"Coefficient\",\n+    na.value = \"grey90\"\n+  ) +\n+  labs(x = NULL, y = NULL) +\n+  theme_minimal(base_size = 11) +\n+  theme(\n+    panel.grid = element_blank(),\n+    strip.text = element_text(face = \"bold\", hjust = 0),\n+    axis.text.y = element_text(size = 9)\n+  )\n+```\n+\n+::: {.callout-warning}\n+## Why the colours cannot be directly compared\n+\n+1. **Different physical magnitudes per tile:** Each row represents a different-sized real-world change. A deep red for `green5km` (a 10 km improvement in green-space proximity) and a deep red for `trans300` (a 600 m improvement in transit distance) look identical on the heatmap but represent interventions that differ by a factor of ~17 in physical distance — and are in different units entirely.\n+\n+2. **Qualitative vs quantitative levels:** The parking rows represent a qualitative step (none → reserved space → reserved garage) with no natural metric. Colour intensity there carries no physical interpretation.\n+\n+3. **Price not on an absolute scale:** The price coefficient — and therefore the Panel B interaction coefficients — is anchored to individual planned costs, not a fixed SEK amount. Comparing the magnitude of `p_green5km` to `p_trans600` on the colour scale is similarly uninformative.\n+\n+4. **What the heatmap IS useful for:** The sign within a single cell tells you the direction of the effect. The most valid cross-cell comparison is within the same row across tenure groups (Owners vs Renters): same physical change, different respondent groups.\n+:::\n+\n ## What can and cannot be read from this grid\n \n **Sign (directional interpretation — valid):** A positive $\\beta_{pa}$ means respondents are *more* price-tolerant when that attribute level is present. A negative value means they are *more* price-sensitive in the presence of that level.\n","language":"diff"}}</script></tool-call></div>

It's doable, but there are a few friction points worth knowing about upfront:

**What needs to change in the YAML:**
- Remove `self-contained: true` and `theme: cosmo` (HTML-only options)
- Switch `format: html` → `format: pdf`

**Potential issues:**

1. **LaTeX engine** — Quarto PDF requires a LaTeX install. If you don't have one, run `tinytex::install_tinytex()` in R. Check first with:
    ```r
    tinytex::is_tinytex()
    ```

2. **`flextable`** — it does support PDF output via LaTeX, but table borders and shading sometimes render slightly differently than in HTML. Worth a visual check after rendering.

3. **Callout blocks** — these render fine in PDF.

4. **The heatmap** — no issues, ggplot2 outputs cleanly to PDF.

The quickest way to try it without losing the HTML version is to add both formats:

```yaml
format:
  html:
    self-contained: true
    toc: true
    toc-depth: 3
    theme: cosmo
  pdf:
    toc: true
    toc-depth: 3
```

Then `quarto render` will produce both. Want me to make that change to the file?
